<img src="0.jpg" alt="Smiley face">

<h2 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en"><strong>Outline of computer science</strong></h2>
<p><strong><a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">Computer science</a></strong>&nbsp;(also called&nbsp;<strong>computing science</strong>) is the study of the theoretical foundations of&nbsp;<a title="Information" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information">information</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computation">computation</a>&nbsp;and their implementation and application in&nbsp;<a title="Computer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer">computer</a>&nbsp;systems. One well known subject classification system for computer science is the&nbsp;<a title="ACM Computing Classification System" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ACM_Computing_Classification_System">ACM Computing Classification System</a>&nbsp;devised by the&nbsp;<a title="Association for Computing Machinery" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Association_for_Computing_Machinery">Association for Computing Machinery</a>.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Contents</strong></p>

<ul>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#What_is_computer_science?"><span class="toctext">What is computer science?</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Subfields"><span class="toctext">Subfields</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#History"><span class="toctext">History</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Professions"><span class="toctext">Professions</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Data_and_data_structures"><span class="toctext">Data and data structures</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><span class="toctext"><a href="#Programming_paradigms">Programming paradigms</a></span></li>
</ul>
<p>&nbsp;</p>

<h2><span id="What_is_computer_science.3F"></span><span id="What_is_computer_science?" class="mw-headline">What is computer science?</span></h2>
<p>Computer science can be described as all of the following:</p>
<ul>
<li><a title="Academic discipline" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academic_discipline">Academic discipline</a></li>
<li><a title="Science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science">Science</a>
<ul>
<li><a title="Applied science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Applied_science">Applied science</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="Subfields" class="mw-headline">Subfields</span></h2>
<h3><span id="Mathematical_foundations" class="mw-headline">Mathematical foundations</span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a title="Coding theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coding_theory">Coding theory</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Useful in networking and other areas where computers communicate with each other.</li>
<li><a title="Game theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Game_theory">Game theory</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Useful in artificial intelligence and&nbsp;<a title="Cybernetics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cybernetics">cybernetics</a>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Discrete Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discrete_Mathematics">Discrete Mathematics</a></li>
<li><a title="Graph theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graph_theory">Graph theory</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Foundations for data structures and searching algorithms.</li>
<li><a title="Mathematical logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_logic">Mathematical logic</a>&nbsp;&ndash;&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Boolean logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boolean_logic">Boolean logic</a>&nbsp;and other ways of&nbsp;<a title="Mathematical model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_model">modeling</a>&nbsp;logical queries; the uses and limitations of formal proof methods</li>
<li><a title="Number theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Number_theory">Number theory</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Theory of the&nbsp;<a title="Integer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Integer">integers</a>. Used in&nbsp;<a title="Cryptography" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptography">cryptography</a>&nbsp;as well as a test domain in&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span id="Algorithms_and_data_structures" class="mw-headline">Algorithms and data structures</span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Algorithms" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithms">Algorithms</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Sequential and parallel computational procedures for solving a wide range of problems.</li>
<li><a title="Data structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_structure">Data structures</a>&nbsp;&ndash; The organization and manipulation of data.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span id="Artificial_intelligence" class="mw-headline">Artificial intelligence</span></h3>
<p><a title="Outline of artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Outline_of_artificial_intelligence">Outline of artificial intelligence</a></p>
<ul>
<li><a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">Artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;&ndash; The implementation and study of systems that exhibit an autonomous intelligence or behavior of their own.</li>
<li><a title="Automated reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automated_reasoning">Automated reasoning</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Solving engines, such as used in&nbsp;<a title="Prolog" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prolog">Prolog</a>, which produce steps to a result given a query on a fact and rule database, and&nbsp;<a title="Automated theorem proving" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automated_theorem_proving">automated theorem provers</a>&nbsp;that aim to prove&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Mathematical theorem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_theorem">mathematical theorems</a>&nbsp;with some assistance from a programmer.</li>
<li><a title="Computer vision" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_vision">Computer vision</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Algorithms for identifying three-dimensional objects from a two-dimensional picture.</li>
<li><a class="new" title="Soft computing (page does not exist)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Soft_computing&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1">Soft computing</a>, the use of inexact solutions for otherwise extremely difficult problems:
<ul>
<li><a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">Machine learning</a>&nbsp;- Automated creation of a set of rules and axioms based on input.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Evolutionary computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_computing">Evolutionary computing</a>&nbsp;- Biologically inspired algorithms.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a title="Natural language processing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language_processing">Natural language processing</a>&nbsp;- Building systems and algorithms that analyze, understand, and generate natural (human) languages.</li>
<li><a title="Robotics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robotics">Robotics</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Algorithms for controlling the behaviour of robots.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span id="Communication_and_security" class="mw-headline">Communication and security</span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Computer networking" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_networking">Networking</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Algorithms and protocols for reliably communicating data across different shared or dedicated media, often including&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Error correction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Error_correction">error correction</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Computer security" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_security">Computer security</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Practical aspects of securing computer systems and computer networks.</li>
<li><a title="Cryptography" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptography">Cryptography</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Applies results from complexity, probability, algebra and number theory to invent and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Cryptoanalysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptoanalysis">break codes</a>, and analyze the security of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Cryptographic protocols" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptographic_protocols">cryptographic protocols</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span id="Computer_architecture" class="mw-headline">Computer architecture</span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a title="Computer architecture" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_architecture">Computer architecture</a>&nbsp;&ndash; The design, organization, optimization and verification of a computer system, mostly about&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="CPU" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CPU">CPUs</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Memory (computers)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Memory_(computers)">Memory</a>&nbsp;subsystem (and the bus connecting them).</li>
<li><a title="Operating system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operating_system">Operating systems</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Systems for managing computer programs and providing the basis of a usable system.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span id="Computer_graphics" class="mw-headline">Computer graphics</span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a title="Computer graphics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_graphics">Computer graphics</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Algorithms both for generating visual images synthetically, and for integrating or altering visual and spatial information sampled from the real world.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Image processing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Image_processing">Image processing</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Determining information from an image through computation.</li>
<li><a title="Information visualization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_visualization">Information visualization</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Methods for representing and displaying abstract data to facilitate human interaction for exploration and understanding.</li>
</ul>

<h3><span id="Concurrent.2C_parallel.2C_and_distributed_systems"></span><span id="Concurrent,_parallel,_and_distributed_systems" class="mw-headline">Concurrent, parallel, and distributed systems</span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a title="Parallel computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parallel_computing">Parallel computing</a>&nbsp;- The theory and practice of simultaneous computation; data safety in any multitasking or multithreaded environment.</li>
<li><a title="Concurrency (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concurrency_(computer_science)">Concurrency (computer science)</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Computing using multiple concurrent threads of execution, devising algorithms for solving problems on multiple processors to achieve maximal speed-up compared to sequential execution.</li>
<li><a title="Distributed computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Distributed_computing">Distributed computing</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Computing using multiple computing devices over a network to accomplish a common objective or task and thereby reducing the latency involved in single processor contributions for any task.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span id="Databases" class="mw-headline">Databases</span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Relational databases" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Relational_databases">Relational databases</a>&nbsp;&ndash; the&nbsp;<a title="Set theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Set_theory">set theoretic</a>&nbsp;and algorithmic foundation of databases.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Structured Storage" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Structured_Storage">Structured Storage</a>&nbsp;- non-relational databases such as&nbsp;<a title="NoSQL" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NoSQL">NoSQL</a>&nbsp;databases.</li>
<li><a title="Data mining" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_mining">Data mining</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Study of algorithms for searching and processing information in documents and databases; closely related to&nbsp;<a title="Information retrieval" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_retrieval">information retrieval</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span id="Programming_languages_and_compilers" class="mw-headline">Programming languages and compilers</span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Compiler theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compiler_theory">Compiler theory</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Theory of&nbsp;<a title="Compiler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compiler">compiler</a>&nbsp;design, based on&nbsp;<a title="Automata theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automata_theory">Automata theory</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language">Programming language pragmatics</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Taxonomy of programming languages, their strength and weaknesses. Various&nbsp;<a title="Programming paradigm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_paradigm">programming paradigms</a>, such as&nbsp;<a title="Object-oriented programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object-oriented_programming">object-oriented programming</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Programming language theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language_theory">Programming language theory</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Formal semantics of programming languages" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_semantics_of_programming_languages">Formal semantics</a>&nbsp;&ndash; rigorous mathematical study of the meaning of programs.</li>
<li><a title="Type theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Type_theory">Type theory</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Formal analysis of the types of data, and the use of these types to understand properties of programs &mdash; especially program safety.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span id="Scientific_computing" class="mw-headline">Scientific computing</span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a title="Computational science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_science">Computational science</a>&nbsp;&ndash; constructing&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Scientific modeling" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific_modeling">mathematical models</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Numerical analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numerical_analysis">quantitative analysis</a>&nbsp;techniques and using computers to analyze and solve&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Scientific" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific">scientific</a>&nbsp;problems.</li>
<li><a title="Numerical analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numerical_analysis">Numerical analysis</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Approximate numerical solution of mathematical problems such as&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Root-finding algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Root-finding_algorithm">root-finding</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Numerical integration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numerical_integration">integration</a>, the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Numerical ordinary differential equations" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numerical_ordinary_differential_equations">solution of ordinary differential equations</a>; the approximation of&nbsp;<a title="Special functions" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_functions">special functions</a>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Symbolic computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symbolic_computation">Symbolic computation</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Manipulation and solution of expressions in symbolic form, also known as&nbsp;<a title="Computer algebra" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_algebra">Computer algebra</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Computational physics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_physics">Computational physics</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Numerical simulations of large non-analytic systems</li>
<li><a title="Computational chemistry" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_chemistry">Computational chemistry</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Computational modelling of theoretical chemistry in order to determine chemical structures and properties</li>
<li><a title="Bioinformatics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bioinformatics">Bioinformatics</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Computational biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_biology">Computational biology</a>&nbsp;&ndash; The use of computer science to maintain, analyse, store&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Biological data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological_data">biological data</a>&nbsp;and to assist in solving biological problems such as&nbsp;<a title="Protein folding" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protein_folding">Protein folding</a>, function prediction and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Phylogeny" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phylogeny">Phylogeny</a>.</li>
<li><a title="Computational neuroscience" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_neuroscience">Computational neuroscience</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Computational modelling of&nbsp;<a title="Neurophysiology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neurophysiology">neurophysiology</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span id="Software_engineering" class="mw-headline">Software engineering</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article:&nbsp;<a title="Outline of software engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Outline_of_software_engineering">Outline of software engineering</a></div>
<ul>
<li><a title="Formal methods" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_methods">Formal methods</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Mathematical approaches for describing and reasoning about software design.</li>
<li><a title="Software engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_engineering">Software engineering</a>&nbsp;&ndash; The principles and practice of designing, developing, and testing programs, as well as proper engineering practices.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Algorithm design" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm_design">Algorithm design</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Using ideas from algorithm theory to creatively design solutions to real tasks.</li>
<li><a title="Computer programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_programming">Computer programming</a>&nbsp;&ndash; The practice of using a programming language to implement algorithms.</li>
<li><a title="Human&ndash;computer interaction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human%E2%80%93computer_interaction">Human&ndash;computer interaction</a>&nbsp;&ndash; The study and design of computer interfaces that people use.</li>
<li><a title="Reverse engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reverse_engineering">Reverse engineering</a>&nbsp;&ndash; The application of the scientific method to the understanding of arbitrary existing software.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span id="Theory_of_computation" class="mw-headline">Theory of computation</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article:&nbsp;<a title="Theory of computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theory_of_computation">Theory of computation</a></div>
<ul>
<li><a title="Automata theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automata_theory">Automata theory</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Different logical structures for solving problems.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Computability theory (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computability_theory_(computer_science)">Computability theory</a>&nbsp;&ndash; What is calculable with the current models of computers. Proofs developed by&nbsp;<a title="Alan Turing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_Turing">Alan Turing</a>&nbsp;and others provide insight into the possibilities of what may be computed and what may not.
<ul>
<li><a title="List of unsolved problems in computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_unsolved_problems_in_computer_science">List of unsolved problems in computer science</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a title="Computational complexity theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_complexity_theory">Computational complexity theory</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Fundamental bounds (especially time and storage space) on classes of computations.</li>
<li><a title="Quantum computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_computing">Quantum computing</a>&nbsp;theory &ndash; Explores computational models involving&nbsp;<a title="Quantum superposition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_superposition">quantum superposition</a>&nbsp;of bits.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="History" class="mw-headline">History</span></h2>
<ul>

</ul>

<ul>
<li><a title="Programmer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programmer">Programmer</a></li>
<li><a title="Teacher" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Teacher">Teacher</a>/<a title="Professor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Professor">Professor</a></li>
<li><a title="Software engineer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_engineer">Software engineer</a></li>
<li><a title="Software architect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_architect">Software architect</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Software developer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_developer">Software developer</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Software tester" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_tester">Software tester</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Hardware engineer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hardware_engineer">Hardware engineer</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Data analyst" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_analyst">Data analyst</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Interaction designer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interaction_designer">Interaction designer</a></li>
<li><a title="Network administrator" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Network_administrator">Network administrator</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="Data_and_data_structures" class="mw-headline">Data and data structures</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="Data structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_structure">Data structure</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Datatype" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Datatype">Data type</a></li>
<li><a title="Associative array" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Associative_array">Associative array</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Hash table" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hash_table">Hash table</a></li>
<li><a title="Array data structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Array_data_structure">Array</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="List (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_(computing)">List</a></li>
<li><a title="Tree (data structure)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tree_(data_structure)">Tree</a></li>
<li><a title="String (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/String_(computer_science)">String</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Matrix (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matrix_(computer_science)">Matrix (computer science)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Databases" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Databases">Database</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="Programming_paradigms" class="mw-headline">Programming paradigms</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a title="Imperative programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperative_programming">Imperative programming</a>/<a title="Procedural programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Procedural_programming">Procedural programming</a></li>
<li><a title="Functional programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Functional_programming">Functional programming</a></li>
<li><a title="Logic programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic_programming">Logic programming</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Object oriented programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object_oriented_programming">Object oriented programming</a>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Class (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_(computer_science)">Class</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Inheritance (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inheritance_(computer_science)">Inheritance</a></li>
<li><a title="Object (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object_(computer_science)">Object</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</br>

<h2><span id="A" class="mw-headline">A</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><strong><a title="Abstract data type" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abstract_data_type">Abstract data type</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (ADT), is a&nbsp;<a title="Mathematical model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_model">mathematical model</a>&nbsp;for&nbsp;<a title="Data type" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_type">data types</a>, where a data type is defined by its behavior (<a title="Semantics (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semantics_(computer_science)">semantics</a>) from the point of view of a&nbsp;<em>user</em>&nbsp;of the data, specifically in terms of possible values, possible operations on data of this type, and the behavior of these operations. This contrasts with&nbsp;<a title="Data structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_structure">data structures</a>, which are concrete representations of data, and are the point of view of an implementer, not a user.</li>
<li><strong><a class="mw-redirect" title="Abstract method" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abstract_method">Abstract method</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is one with only a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Method signature" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Method_signature">signature</a>&nbsp;and no&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Method body" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Method_body">implementation body</a>. It is often used to specify that a subclass must provide an implementation of the method. Abstract methods are used to specify&nbsp;<a title="Interface (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interface_(computing)">interfaces</a>&nbsp;in some computer languages.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a class="mw-redirect" title="Abstraction (software engineering)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abstraction_(software_engineering)">Abstraction</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Software engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_engineering">software engineering</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>, abstraction is:
<ul>
<li>the process of removing physical, spatial, or temporal details<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Attribute (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attribute_(computing)">attributes</a>&nbsp;in the study of objects or&nbsp;<a title="System" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/System">systems</a>&nbsp;in order to more closely attend to other details of interest;<sup id="cite_ref-abstraction_3-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;it is also very similar in nature to the process of&nbsp;<a title="Generalization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Generalization">generalization</a>;</li>
<li>the&nbsp;<a title="Abstract and concrete" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abstract_and_concrete">abstract</a>&nbsp;<a title="Concept" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concept">concept</a>-<a title="Object (philosophy)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object_(philosophy)">objects</a>&nbsp;which are created by keeping common features or attributes to various concrete objects or systems of study<sup id="cite_ref-abstraction_3-1" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;&mdash; the result of the process of abstraction.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong><a title="Agent architecture" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agent_architecture">Agent architecture</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Blueprint" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blueprint">blueprint</a>&nbsp;for&nbsp;<a title="Software agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_agent">software agents</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Intelligent control" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligent_control">intelligent control</a>&nbsp;systems, depicting the arrangement of components. The architectures implemented by&nbsp;<a title="Intelligent agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligent_agent">intelligent agents</a>&nbsp;are referred to as&nbsp;<a title="Cognitive architecture" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive_architecture">cognitive architectures</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Agent-based model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agent-based_model">Agent-based model</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (ABM), is a class of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computational models" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_models">computational models</a>&nbsp;for&nbsp;<a title="Computer simulation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_simulation">simulating</a>&nbsp;the actions and interactions of autonomous agents (both individual or collective entities such as organizations or groups) with a view to assessing their effects on the system as a whole. It combines elements of&nbsp;<a title="Game theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Game_theory">game theory</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Complex systems" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Complex_systems">complex systems</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Emergence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emergence">emergence</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Computational sociology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_sociology">computational sociology</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Multi-agent system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multi-agent_system">multi-agent systems</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Evolutionary programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_programming">evolutionary programming</a>.&nbsp;<a title="Monte Carlo method" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monte_Carlo_method">Monte Carlo methods</a>&nbsp;are used to introduce randomness.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Aggregate function" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aggregate_function">Aggregate function</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Database management" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Database_management">database management</a>&nbsp;an aggregate function is a&nbsp;<a title="Subroutine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subroutine">function</a>&nbsp;where the values of multiple rows are grouped together to form a single value of more significant meaning or measurement such as a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Set (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Set_(computer_science)">set</a>, a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Set (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Set_(computer_science)#Multiset">bag</a>&nbsp;or a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="List (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_(computing)">list</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Agile software development" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agile_software_development">Agile software development</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is an approach to&nbsp;<a title="Software development" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_development">software development</a>&nbsp;under which requirements and solutions evolve through the collaborative effort of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Self-organizing communities" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-organizing_communities">self-organizing</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Cross-functional team" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cross-functional_team">cross-functional</a>&nbsp;teams and their&nbsp;<a title="Customer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Customer">customer(s)</a>/<a title="End user" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/End_user">end user(s)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Collier_2011_5-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;It advocates adaptive planning, evolutionary development, early delivery, and&nbsp;<a title="Continual improvement process" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continual_improvement_process">continual improvement</a>, and it encourages rapid and flexible response to change.<sup id="cite_ref-WhatIsAgile_6-0" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">Algorithm</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is an unambiguous specification of how to solve a class of problems. Algorithms can perform&nbsp;<a title="Calculation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calculation">calculation</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Data processing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_processing">data processing</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Automated reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automated_reasoning">automated reasoning</a>&nbsp;tasks.</li>
<li><strong><a class="mw-redirect" title="Algorithm design" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm_design">Algorithm design</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; refers to a method or mathematical process for problem solving and engineering algorithms. The design of algorithms is part of many solution theories of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Operation research" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_research">operation research</a>, such as&nbsp;<a title="Dynamic programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dynamic_programming">dynamic programming</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Divide and conquer algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Divide_and_conquer_algorithm">divide-and-conquer</a>. Techniques for designing and implementing algorithm designs are also called algorithm design patterns,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;such as the template method pattern and decorator pattern.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Algorithmic efficiency" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithmic_efficiency">Algorithmic efficiency</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a property of an&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithm</a>&nbsp;which relates to the number of&nbsp;<a title="Computational resource" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_resource">computational resources</a>&nbsp;used by the algorithm. An algorithm must be&nbsp;<a title="Analysis of algorithms" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Analysis_of_algorithms">analyzed</a>&nbsp;to determine its resource usage, and the efficiency of an algorithm can be measured based on usage of different resources. Algorithmic efficiency can be thought of as analogous to engineering&nbsp;<a title="Productivity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Productivity">productivity</a>&nbsp;for a repeating or continuous process.</li>
<li><strong><a title="ASCII" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ASCII">ASCII</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; abbreviated from&nbsp;<strong>American Standard Code for Information Interchange</strong>, is a&nbsp;<a title="Character encoding" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Character_encoding">character encoding</a>&nbsp;standard for electronic communication. ASCII codes represent text in computers,&nbsp;<a title="Telecommunications equipment" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telecommunications_equipment">telecommunications equipment</a>, and other devices. Most modern character-encoding schemes are based on ASCII, although they support many additional characters.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Application programming interface" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface">Application programming interface</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (API) is a set of subroutine definitions,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Communication protocols" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communication_protocols">communication protocols</a>, and tools for building software. In general terms, it is a set of clearly defined methods of communication among various components. A good API makes it easier to develop a&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">computer program</a>&nbsp;by providing all the building blocks, which are then put together by the&nbsp;<a title="Programmer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programmer">programmer</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Application software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_software">Application software</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (app or application for short) is&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computer software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_software">computer software</a>&nbsp;designed to perform a group of coordinated functions, tasks, or activities for the benefit of the user. Examples of an application include a&nbsp;<a title="Word processor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Word_processor">word processor</a>, a&nbsp;<a title="Spreadsheet" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spreadsheet">spreadsheet</a>, an&nbsp;<a title="Accounting software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Accounting_software">accounting application</a>, a&nbsp;<a title="Web browser" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_browser">web browser</a>, a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Media player (software)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Media_player_(software)">media player</a>, an aeronautical&nbsp;<a title="Flight simulator" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flight_simulator">flight simulator</a>, a&nbsp;<a title="Console game" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Console_game">console game</a>&nbsp;or a&nbsp;<a title="Raster graphics editor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raster_graphics_editor">photo editor</a>. The&nbsp;<a title="Collective noun" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collective_noun">collective noun</a>&nbsp;application software refers to all applications collectively.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;This contrasts with&nbsp;<a title="System software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/System_software">system software</a>, which is mainly involved with running the computer.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Array data structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Array_data_structure">Array data structure</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; or simply an array, is a&nbsp;<a title="Data structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_structure">data structure</a>&nbsp;consisting of a collection of&nbsp;<em>elements</em>&nbsp;(<a title="Value (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Value_(computer_science)">values</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Variable (programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variable_(programming)">variables</a>), each identified by at least one&nbsp;<em>array index</em>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<em>key</em>. An array is stored such that the position of each element can be computed from its index&nbsp;<a title="Tuple" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tuple">tuple</a>&nbsp;by a mathematical formula.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-andres_10-0" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-garcia_11-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;The simplest type of data structure is a linear array, also called one-dimensional array.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Artifact (software development)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artifact_(software_development)">Artifact</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is one of many kinds of tangible by-products produced during the development of software. Some artifacts (e.g.,&nbsp;<a title="Use case" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Use_case">use cases</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Class diagram" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_diagram">class diagrams</a>, and other&nbsp;<a title="Unified Modeling Language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unified_Modeling_Language">Unified Modeling Language</a>&nbsp;(UML) models, requirements and design documents) help describe the function, architecture, and design of software. Other artifacts are concerned with the process of development itself&mdash;such as project plans, business cases, and risk assessments.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">Artificial intelligence</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (AI), sometimes called&nbsp;<a title="Machine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine">machine</a>&nbsp;intelligence, is&nbsp;<a title="Intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligence">intelligence</a>&nbsp;demonstrated by&nbsp;<a title="Machine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine">machines</a>, in contrast to the&nbsp;<strong><a class="mw-redirect" title="Natural" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural">natural</a>&nbsp;intelligence</strong>&nbsp;displayed by humans and other animals. In&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>&nbsp;AI research is defined as the study of "<a title="Intelligent agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligent_agent">intelligent agents</a>": any device that perceives its environment and takes actions that maximize its chance of successfully achieving its goals.<sup id="cite_ref-Definition_of_AI_12-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;Colloquially, the term "artificial intelligence" is applied when a machine mimics "cognitive" functions that humans associate with other&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Human mind" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_mind">human minds</a>, such as "learning" and "problem solving".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERussellNorvig20092_13-0" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="ASCII" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ASCII">ASCII</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; American Standard Code for Information Interchange.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Assertion (software development)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assertion_(software_development)">Assertion</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computer programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_programming">computer programming</a>, an assertion is a&nbsp;<a title="Statement (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statement_(computer_science)">statement</a>&nbsp;that a&nbsp;<a title="Predicate (mathematical logic)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Predicate_(mathematical_logic)">predicate</a>&nbsp;(<a title="Boolean-valued function" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boolean-valued_function">Boolean-valued function</a>, i.e. a true&ndash;false&nbsp;<a title="Expression (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expression_(computer_science)">expression</a>) is always true at that point in code execution. It can help a programmer read the code, help a compiler compile it, or help the program detect its own defects. For the latter, some programs check assertions by actually evaluating the predicate as they run and if it is not in fact true, an assertion failure, the program considers itself to be broken and typically deliberately&nbsp;<a title="Crash (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crash_(computing)">crashes</a>&nbsp;or throws an assertion failure&nbsp;<a title="Exception handling" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exception_handling">exception</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Associative array" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Associative_array">Associative array</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Automata theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automata_theory">Automata theory</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is the study of&nbsp;<a title="Abstract machine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abstract_machine">abstract machines</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Automaton" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automaton">automata</a>, as well as the&nbsp;<a title="Computational problem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_problem">computational problems</a>&nbsp;that can be solved using them. It is a theory in&nbsp;<a title="Theoretical computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theoretical_computer_science">theoretical computer science</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Discrete mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discrete_mathematics">discrete mathematics</a>&nbsp;(a subject of study in both&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>). The word&nbsp;<em>automata</em>&nbsp;(the plural of&nbsp;<em>automaton</em>) comes from the Greek word &alpha;ὐ&tau;ό&mu;&alpha;&tau;&alpha;, which means "self-acting".</li>
<li><strong><a title="Automated reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automated_reasoning">Automated reasoning</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is an area of&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Mathematical logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_logic">mathematical logic</a>&nbsp;dedicated to understanding different aspects of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reasoning">reasoning</a>. The study of automated reasoning helps produce&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computer programs" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_programs">computer programs</a>&nbsp;that allow computers to reason completely, or nearly completely, automatically. Although automated reasoning is considered a sub-field of&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>, it also has connections with&nbsp;<a title="Theoretical computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theoretical_computer_science">theoretical computer science</a>, and even&nbsp;<a title="Philosophy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosophy">philosophy</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="B" class="mw-headline">B</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><strong><a title="Bandwidth (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bandwidth_(computing)">Bandwidth</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is the maximum rate of data transfer across a given path. Bandwidth may be characterized as&nbsp;<strong>network bandwidth</strong>,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;<strong>data bandwidth</strong>,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<strong>digital bandwidth</strong>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Bayesian programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bayesian_programming">Bayesian programming</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a formalism and a methodology for having a technique to specify&nbsp;<a title="Probability distribution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Probability_distribution">probabilistic models</a>&nbsp;and solve problems when less than the necessary information is available.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Benchmark (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benchmark_(computing)">Benchmark</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is the act of running a&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">computer program</a>, a set of programs, or other operations, in order to assess the relative&nbsp;<strong>performance</strong>&nbsp;of an object, normally by running a number of standard tests and trials against it.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;The term&nbsp;<em>benchmark</em>&nbsp;is also commonly utilized for the purposes of elaborately designed benchmarking programs themselves.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Best, worst and average case" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Best,_worst_and_average_case">Best, worst and average case</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;&nbsp;<strong>best</strong>,&nbsp;<strong>worst,</strong>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<strong>average cases</strong>&nbsp;of a given&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithm</a>&nbsp;express what the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Resource (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resource_(computer_science)">resource</a>&nbsp;usage is&nbsp;<em>at least</em>,&nbsp;<em>at most</em>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<em>on average</em>, respectively. Usually the resource being considered is running time, i.e.&nbsp;<a title="Time complexity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_complexity">time complexity</a>, but it could also be memory or other resource. Best case is the function which performs the minimum number of steps on input data of n elements. Worst case is the function which performs the maximum number of steps on input data of size n. Average case is the function which performs an average number of steps on input data of n elements.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Big data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_data">Big data</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a term used to refer to&nbsp;<a title="Data set" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_set">data sets</a>&nbsp;that are too large or complex for traditional&nbsp;<a title="Data processing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_processing">data-processing</a>&nbsp;<a title="Application software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_software">application software</a>&nbsp;to adequately deal with. Data with many cases (rows) offer greater&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Statistical power" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_power">statistical power</a>, while data with higher complexity (more attributes or columns) may lead to a higher&nbsp;<a title="False discovery rate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/False_discovery_rate">false discovery rate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Big O notation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_O_notation">Big O notation</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a mathematical notation that describes the&nbsp;<a title="Asymptotic analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asymptotic_analysis">limiting behavior</a>&nbsp;of a&nbsp;<a title="Function (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Function_(mathematics)">function</a>&nbsp;when the argument tends towards a particular value or infinity. It is a member of a family of notations invented by&nbsp;<a title="Paul Gustav Heinrich Bachmann" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Gustav_Heinrich_Bachmann">Paul Bachmann</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Bachmann_20-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;<a title="Edmund Landau" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edmund_Landau">Edmund Landau</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Landau_21-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;and others, collectively called&nbsp;<strong>Bachmann&ndash;Landau notation</strong>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<strong>asymptotic notation</strong>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Binary number" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Binary_number">Binary number</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In mathematics and&nbsp;<a title="Digital electronics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_electronics">digital electronics</a>, a&nbsp;<strong>binary number</strong>&nbsp;is a&nbsp;<a title="Number" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Number">number</a>&nbsp;expressed in the&nbsp;<strong>base-2 numeral system</strong>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<strong>binary numeral system</strong>, which uses only two symbols: typically&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="0 (number)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/0_(number)">0 (zero)</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="1 (number)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1_(number)">1 (one)</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Binary search algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Binary_search_algorithm">Binary search algorithm</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;&nbsp;<strong>binary search</strong>, also known as&nbsp;<strong>half-interval search</strong>,<sup id="cite_ref-Williams1976_22-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;<strong>logarithmic search</strong>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKnuth1998&sect;6.2.1_(&quot;Searching_an_ordered_table&quot;),_subsection_&quot;Binary_search&quot;_23-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<strong>binary chop</strong>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEButterfieldNgondi201646_24-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;is a&nbsp;<a title="Search algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Search_algorithm">search algorithm</a>&nbsp;that finds the position of a target value within a&nbsp;<a title="Sorted array" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sorted_array">sorted array</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECormenLeisersonRivestStein200939_25-0" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Binary tree" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Binary_tree">Binary tree</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Tree structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tree_structure">tree</a>&nbsp;<a title="Data structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_structure">data structure</a>&nbsp;in which each node has at most two&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Child node" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Child_node">children</a>, which are referred to as the&nbsp;<em><span id="left_child">left child</span></em>&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<em><span id="right_child">right child</span></em>. A&nbsp;<a title="Recursive definition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recursive_definition">recursive definition</a>&nbsp;using just&nbsp;<a title="Set theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Set_theory">set theory</a>&nbsp;notions is that a (non-empty) binary tree is a&nbsp;<a title="Tuple" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tuple">tuple</a>&nbsp;(<em>L</em>,&nbsp;<em>S</em>,&nbsp;<em>R</em>), where&nbsp;<em>L</em>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<em>R</em>&nbsp;are binary trees or the&nbsp;<a title="Empty set" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empty_set">empty set</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<em>S</em>&nbsp;is a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Singleton set" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Singleton_set">singleton set</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GarnierTaylor2009_27-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;Some authors allow the binary tree to be the empty set as well.<sup id="cite_ref-Skiena2009_28-0" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Bioinformatics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bioinformatics">Bioinformatics</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Interdisciplinary" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interdisciplinary">interdisciplinary</a>&nbsp;field that develops methods and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Software tool" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_tool">software tools</a>&nbsp;for understanding&nbsp;<a title="Biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biology">biological</a>&nbsp;data. As an interdisciplinary field of science, bioinformatics combines&nbsp;<a title="Biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biology">biology</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Information engineering (field)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_engineering_(field)">information engineering</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Statistics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistics">statistics</a>&nbsp;to analyze and interpret biological data. Bioinformatics has been used for&nbsp;<em><a title="In silico" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/In_silico">in silico</a></em>&nbsp;analyses of biological queries using mathematical and statistical techniques.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Bit" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bit">Bit</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (a&nbsp;<a title="Portmanteau" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portmanteau">portmanteau</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<strong>binary digit</strong>)<sup id="cite_ref-Mackenzie_1980_29-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;is a&nbsp;<a title="Units of information" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Units_of_information">basic unit</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Information" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information">information</a>&nbsp;used in&nbsp;<a title="Computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computing">computing</a>&nbsp;and digital&nbsp;<a title="Communication" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communication">communications</a>. A&nbsp;<a title="Binary number" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Binary_number">binary</a>&nbsp;digit can have only one of two&nbsp;<a title="Value (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Value_(computer_science)">values</a>, and may be physically represented with a two-state device. These state values are most commonly represented as either a&nbsp;0or1.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Bit rate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bit_rate">Bit rate</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Telecommunications" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telecommunications">telecommunications</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computing">computing</a>,&nbsp;<strong>bit rate</strong>&nbsp;(<strong>bitrate</strong>&nbsp;or as a variable&nbsp;<em>R</em>) is the number of&nbsp;<a title="Bit" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bit">bits</a>&nbsp;that are conveyed or processed per unit of time.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Blacklist (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blacklist_(computing)">Blacklist</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computing">computing</a>, a&nbsp;<strong>blacklist</strong>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<strong>block list</strong>&nbsp;is a basic&nbsp;<a title="Access control" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Access_control">access control</a>&nbsp;mechanism that allows through all elements (email addresses, users, passwords,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="URLs" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/URLs">URLs</a>,&nbsp;<a title="IP address" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IP_address">IP addresses</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Domain name" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domain_name">domain names</a>, file&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="MD5 Hash" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MD5_Hash">hashes</a>, etc.), except those explicitly mentioned. Those items on the list are denied access. The opposite is a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Whitelist" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Whitelist">whitelist</a>, which means only items on the list are let through whatever gate is being used. A&nbsp;<a title="Greylisting (email)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greylisting_(email)">greylist</a>&nbsp;contains items that are temporarily blocked (or temporarily allowed) until an additional step is performed.</li>
<li><strong><a title="BMP file format" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BMP_file_format">BMP file format</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; also known as&nbsp;<strong>bitmap image file</strong>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<strong>device independent bitmap (DIB) file format</strong>&nbsp;or simply a&nbsp;<strong>bitmap</strong>, is a&nbsp;<a title="Raster graphics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raster_graphics">raster graphics</a>&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Image file format" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Image_file_format">image file format</a>&nbsp;used to store&nbsp;<a title="Bitmap" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bitmap">bitmap</a>&nbsp;<a title="Digital image" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_image">digital images</a>, independently of the&nbsp;<a title="Display device" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Display_device">display device</a>&nbsp;(such as a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Graphics adapter" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graphics_adapter">graphics adapter</a>), especially on&nbsp;<a title="Microsoft Windows" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsoft_Windows">Microsoft Windows</a><sup id="cite_ref-bmp_31-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="OS/2" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OS/2">OS/2</a><sup id="cite_ref-os2bmp_32-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;operating systems.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Boolean data type" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boolean_data_type">Boolean data type</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Data type" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_type">data type</a>&nbsp;that has one of two possible values (usually denoted&nbsp;<em>true</em>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<em>false</em>), intended to represent the two&nbsp;<a title="Truth value" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Truth_value">truth values</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic">logic</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Boolean algebra" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boolean_algebra">Boolean algebra</a>. It is named after&nbsp;<a title="George Boole" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Boole">George Boole</a>, who first defined an algebraic system of logic in the mid 19th century. The Boolean data type is primarily associated with&nbsp;<a title="Conditional (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conditional_(computer_programming)">conditional</a>&nbsp;statements, which allow different actions by changing&nbsp;<a title="Control flow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_flow">control flow</a>&nbsp;depending on whether a programmer-specified Boolean&nbsp;<em>condition</em>&nbsp;evaluates to true or false. It is a special case of a more general&nbsp;<em>logical data type (see&nbsp;<a title="Probabilistic logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Probabilistic_logic">probabilistic logic</a>)&mdash;</em>logic need not always be Boolean.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Boolean expression" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boolean_expression">Boolean expression</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is used&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Expression (programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expression_(programming)">expression</a>&nbsp;in a&nbsp;<a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language">programming language</a>&nbsp;that produces a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Boolean value" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boolean_value">Boolean value</a>&nbsp;when evaluated, that is one of&nbsp;<strong>true</strong>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<strong>false</strong>. A Boolean expression may be composed of a combination of the Boolean constants&nbsp;<strong>true</strong>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<strong>false</strong>,&nbsp;<a title="Boolean data type" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boolean_data_type">Boolean-typed</a>&nbsp;variables, Boolean-valued operators, and&nbsp;<a title="Boolean-valued function" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boolean-valued_function">Boolean-valued functions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Boolean algebra" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boolean_algebra">Boolean algebra</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Mathematical logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_logic">mathematical logic</a>,&nbsp;<strong>Boolean algebra</strong>&nbsp;is the branch of&nbsp;<a title="Algebra" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algebra">algebra</a>&nbsp;in which the values of the&nbsp;<a title="Variable (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variable_(mathematics)">variables</a>&nbsp;are the&nbsp;<a title="Truth value" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Truth_value">truth values</a>&nbsp;<em>true</em>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<em>false</em>, usually denoted 1 and 0 respectively. Instead of&nbsp;<a title="Elementary algebra" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elementary_algebra">elementary algebra</a>&nbsp;where the values of the variables are numbers, and the prime operations are addition and multiplication, the main operations of Boolean algebra are the&nbsp;<a title="Logical conjunction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logical_conjunction">conjunction</a>&nbsp;<em>and</em>&nbsp;denoted as &and;, the&nbsp;<a title="Logical disjunction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logical_disjunction">disjunction</a>&nbsp;<em>or</em>&nbsp;denoted as &or;, and the&nbsp;<a title="Negation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negation">negation</a>&nbsp;<em>not</em>&nbsp;denoted as &not;. It is thus a formalism for describing logical relations in the same way that elementary algebra describes numeric relations.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Byte" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byte">Byte</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Units of information" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Units_of_information">unit of digital information</a>&nbsp;that most commonly consists of eight&nbsp;<a title="Bit" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bit">bits</a>, representing a&nbsp;<a title="Binary number" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Binary_number">binary number</a>. Historically, the byte was the number of bits used to encode a single&nbsp;<a title="Character (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Character_(computing)">character</a>&nbsp;of text in a computer<sup id="cite_ref-Buchholz_1962_34-0" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bemer_1959_35-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;and for this reason it is the smallest&nbsp;<a title="Address space" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Address_space">addressable</a>&nbsp;unit of&nbsp;<a title="Computer memory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_memory">memory</a>&nbsp;in many&nbsp;<a title="Computer architecture" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_architecture">computer architectures</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Booting" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Booting">Booting</a></strong>- is starting up a&nbsp;<a title="Computer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer">computer</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Computer appliance" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_appliance">computer appliance</a>&nbsp;until it can be used. It can be initiated by hardware such as a button press or by software command. After the power is switched on, the computer is relatively dumb and can read only part of its storage called&nbsp;<a title="Read-only memory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Read-only_memory">read-only memory</a>. There, a small program is stored called&nbsp;<a title="Firmware" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Firmware">firmware</a>. It does&nbsp;<a title="Power-on self-test" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Power-on_self-test">power-on self-tests</a>&nbsp;and, most importantly, allows accessing other types of memory like a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Hard disk" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hard_disk">hard disk</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Main memory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Main_memory">main memory</a>. The firmware loads bigger&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">programs</a>&nbsp;into the computer's&nbsp;<a title="Random-access memory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Random-access_memory">main memory</a>&nbsp;and runs it.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="C" class="mw-headline">C</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><strong><a title="Callback (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Callback_(computer_programming)">Callback</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; also known as a "call-after<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;" function, is any&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Executable code" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executable_code">executable code</a>&nbsp;that is passed as an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Argument (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Argument_(computer_science)">argument</a>&nbsp;to other code that is expected to&nbsp;<em>call back</em>&nbsp;(execute) the argument at a given time. This execution may be immediate as in a&nbsp;<strong>synchronous callback</strong>, or it might happen at a later time as in an&nbsp;<strong>asynchronous callback</strong>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Central processing unit" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_processing_unit">Central processing unit</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (<strong>CPU</strong>) is the&nbsp;<a title="Electronic circuit" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electronic_circuit">electronic circuitry</a>&nbsp;within a&nbsp;<a title="Computer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer">computer</a>&nbsp;that carries out the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Instruction (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instruction_(computing)">instructions</a>&nbsp;of a&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">computer program</a>&nbsp;by performing the basic&nbsp;<a title="Arithmetic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arithmetic">arithmetic</a>, logic, controlling and&nbsp;<a title="Input/output" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Input/output">input/output</a>&nbsp;(I/O) operations specified by the instructions. The computer industry has used the term "central processing unit" at least since the early 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-weik1961_37-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;Traditionally, the term "CPU" refers to a&nbsp;<strong>processor</strong>, more specifically to its processing unit and&nbsp;<a title="Control unit" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_unit">control unit</a>&nbsp;(CU), distinguishing these core elements of a computer from external components such as&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Main memory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Main_memory">main memory</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="I/O" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/I/O">I/O</a>&nbsp;circuitry.<sup id="cite_ref-kuck_38-0" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Character (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Character_(computing)">Character</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer">computer</a>&nbsp;and machine-based&nbsp;<a title="Telecommunication" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telecommunication">telecommunications</a>&nbsp;terminology, a&nbsp;<strong>character</strong>&nbsp;is a unit of&nbsp;<a title="Information" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information">information</a>&nbsp;that roughly corresponds to a&nbsp;<a title="Grapheme" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grapheme">grapheme</a>, grapheme-like unit, or symbol, such as in an&nbsp;<a title="Alphabet" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alphabet">alphabet</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Syllabary" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syllabary">syllabary</a>&nbsp;in the&nbsp;<a title="Written language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Written_language">written</a>&nbsp;form of a&nbsp;<a title="Natural language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language">natural language</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Cipher" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cipher">Cipher</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Cryptography" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptography">cryptography</a>, a&nbsp;<strong>cipher</strong>&nbsp;(or&nbsp;<strong>cypher</strong>) is an&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithm</a>&nbsp;for performing&nbsp;<a title="Encryption" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Encryption">encryption</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Decryption" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decryption">decryption</a>&mdash;a series of well-defined steps that can be followed as a procedure.</li>
<li><strong><a class="mw-redirect" title="Class (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_(computer_science)">Class</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Object-oriented programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object-oriented_programming">object-oriented programming</a>, a&nbsp;<strong>class</strong>&nbsp;is an extensible program-code-template for creating&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Object (object-oriented programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object_(object-oriented_programming)">objects</a>, providing initial values for state (<a title="Member variable" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Member_variable">member variables</a>) and implementations of behavior (member functions or&nbsp;<a title="Method (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Method_(computer_programming)">methods</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGammaHelmJohnsonVlissides199514_40-0" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce20022.1_Objects,_classes,_and_object_types,_https://books.google.com/books?id=9NGWq3K1RwUC&amp;pg=PA18_41-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;In many languages, the class name is used as the name for the class (the template itself), the name for the default&nbsp;<a title="Constructor (object-oriented programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constructor_(object-oriented_programming)">constructor</a>&nbsp;of the class (a&nbsp;<a title="Subroutine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subroutine">subroutine</a>&nbsp;that creates objects), and as the&nbsp;<a title="Data type" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_type">type</a>&nbsp;of objects generated by&nbsp;<a title="Instance (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instance_(computer_science)">instantiating</a>&nbsp;the class; these distinct concepts are easily conflated.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce20022.1_Objects,_classes,_and_object_types,_https://books.google.com/books?id=9NGWq3K1RwUC&amp;pg=PA18_41-1" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Class-based programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class-based_programming">Class-based programming</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; or more commonly&nbsp;<strong>class-orientation</strong>, is a style of&nbsp;<a title="Object-oriented programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object-oriented_programming">Object-oriented programming</a>&nbsp;(OOP) in which inheritance occurs via defining&nbsp;<em><a title="Class (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_(computer_programming)">classes</a></em>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Object (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object_(computer_science)">objects</a>, instead of inheritance occurring via the objects alone (compare&nbsp;<a title="Prototype-based programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prototype-based_programming">prototype-based programming</a>).</li>
<li><strong><a title="Class-based programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class-based_programming">Class-orientation</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a style of&nbsp;<a title="Object-oriented programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object-oriented_programming">Object-oriented programming</a>&nbsp;(OOP) in which inheritance occurs via defining&nbsp;<em><a title="Class (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_(computer_programming)">classes</a></em>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Object (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object_(computer_science)">objects</a>, instead of inheritance occurring via the objects alone (compare&nbsp;<a title="Prototype-based programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prototype-based_programming">prototype-based programming</a>).</li>
<li><strong><a title="Client (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Client_(computing)">Client</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a piece of&nbsp;<a title="Computer hardware" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_hardware">computer hardware</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software">software</a>&nbsp;that accesses a service made available by a&nbsp;<a title="Server (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Server_(computing)">server</a>. The server is often (but not always) on another&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computer system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_system">computer system</a>, in which case the client accesses the service by way of a&nbsp;<a title="Computer network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_network">network</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;The term applies to the role that programs or devices play in the&nbsp;<a title="Client&ndash;server model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Client%E2%80%93server_model">client&ndash;server model</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Cleanroom software engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cleanroom_software_engineering">Cleanroom software engineering</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Software development process" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_development_process">software development process</a>&nbsp;intended to produce software with a certifiable level of&nbsp;<a title="Reliability engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reliability_engineering">reliability</a>. The cleanroom process was originally developed by&nbsp;<a title="Harlan Mills" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harlan_Mills">Harlan Mills</a>&nbsp;and several of his colleagues including Alan Hevner at&nbsp;<a title="IBM" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IBM">IBM</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;The focus of the cleanroom process is on defect prevention, rather than defect removal.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Closure (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Closure_(computer_programming)">Closure</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language">programming languages</a>, a&nbsp;<strong>closure</strong>&nbsp;(also&nbsp;<strong>lexical closure</strong>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<strong>function closure</strong>) is a technique for implementing&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Lexically scoped" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lexically_scoped">lexically scoped</a>&nbsp;<a title="Name binding" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Name_binding">name binding</a>&nbsp;in a language with&nbsp;<a title="First-class function" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First-class_function">first-class functions</a>.&nbsp;<a title="Operational semantics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operational_semantics">Operationally</a>, a closure is a&nbsp;<a title="Record (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Record_(computer_science)">record</a>&nbsp;storing a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Function (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Function_(computer_science)">function</a><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_computer_science#cite_note-44">[a]</a></sup>&nbsp;together with an environment.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Cloud computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cloud_computing">Cloud computing</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is shared pools of configurable computer&nbsp;<a title="System resource" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/System_resource">system resources</a>&nbsp;and higher-level services that can be rapidly&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Provisioning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Provisioning">provisioned</a>&nbsp;with minimal management effort, often over the&nbsp;<a title="Internet" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet">Internet</a>. Cloud computing relies on sharing of resources to achieve coherence and&nbsp;<a title="Economies of scale" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economies_of_scale">economies of scale</a>, similar to a&nbsp;<a title="Public utility" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_utility">public utility</a>.</li>
