<li><strong><a title="Library (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Library_(computing)">Code library</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a collection of&nbsp;<a title="Non-volatile memory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-volatile_memory">non-volatile resources</a>&nbsp;used by&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">computer programs</a>, often for&nbsp;<a title="Software development" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_development">software development</a>. These may include configuration data, documentation, help data, message templates,&nbsp;<a title="Code reuse" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Code_reuse">pre-written code</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Subroutine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subroutine">subroutines</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Class (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_(computer_science)">classes</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Value (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Value_(computer_science)">values</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Data type" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_type">type</a>&nbsp;specifications. In&nbsp;<a title="OS/360 and successors" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OS/360_and_successors">IBM's OS/360 and its successors</a>&nbsp;they are referred to as&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Partitioned dataset" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partitioned_dataset">partitioned data sets</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Computer programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_programming">Coding</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; Computer programming is the process of designing and building an&nbsp;<a title="Executable" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executable">executable</a>&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">computer program</a>&nbsp;for accomplishing a specific&nbsp;<a title="Computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computing">computing</a>&nbsp;task. Programming involves tasks such as analysis, generating&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithms</a>, profiling algorithms' accuracy and resource consumption, and the implementation of algorithms in a chosen&nbsp;<a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language">programming language</a>&nbsp;(commonly referred to as&nbsp;<strong>coding</strong><sup id="cite_ref-tumblr2014_46-0" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tumblr1_47-0" class="reference"></sup>). The&nbsp;<a title="Source code" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Source_code">source code</a>&nbsp;of a program is written in one or more programming languages. The purpose of programming is to find a sequence of instructions that will automate the performance of a task for solving a given problem. The process of programming thus often requires expertise in several different subjects, including knowledge of the&nbsp;<a title="Domain (software engineering)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domain_(software_engineering)">application domain</a>, specialized algorithms, and formal&nbsp;<a title="Logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic">logic</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Coding theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coding_theory">Coding theory</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is the study of the properties of&nbsp;<a title="Code" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Code">codes</a>&nbsp;and their respective fitness for specific applications. Codes are used for&nbsp;<a title="Data compression" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_compression">data compression</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Cryptography" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptography">cryptography</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Error detection and correction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Error_detection_and_correction">error detection and correction</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Data transmission" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_transmission">data transmission</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Data storage" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_storage">data storage</a>. Codes are studied by various scientific disciplines&mdash;such as&nbsp;<a title="Information theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_theory">information theory</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Electrical engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrical_engineering">electrical engineering</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Linguistics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linguistics">linguistics</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>&mdash;for the purpose of designing efficient and reliable data transmission methods. This typically involves the removal of redundancy and the correction or detection of errors in the transmitted data.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Cognitive science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive_science">Cognitive science</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is the interdisciplinary,&nbsp;<a title="Science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science">scientific</a>&nbsp;study of the&nbsp;<a title="Mind" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mind">mind</a>&nbsp;and its processes.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;It examines the nature, the tasks, and the functions of&nbsp;<a title="Cognition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognition">cognition</a>&nbsp;(in a broad sense). Cognitive scientists study intelligence and behavior, with a focus on how nervous systems represent, process, and transform&nbsp;<a title="Information" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information">information</a>. Mental faculties of concern to cognitive scientists include&nbsp;<a title="Language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Language">language</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Perception" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perception">perception</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Memory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Memory">memory</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Attention" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attention">attention</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reasoning">reasoning</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Emotion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emotion">emotion</a>; to understand these faculties, cognitive scientists borrow from fields such as&nbsp;<a title="Linguistics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linguistics">linguistics</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Psychology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Psychology">psychology</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Philosophy of mind" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosophy_of_mind">philosophy</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Neuroscience" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuroscience">neuroscience</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Anthropology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anthropology">anthropology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-stanford1_49-0" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Comma-separated values" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comma-separated_values">Comma-separated values</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (<strong>CSV</strong>)&nbsp;<a title="Computer file" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_file">file</a>&nbsp;is a delimited&nbsp;<a title="Text file" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Text_file">text file</a>&nbsp;that uses a comma to separate values. A CSV file stores&nbsp;<a title="Table (information)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Table_(information)">tabular</a>&nbsp;data (numbers and text) in&nbsp;<a title="Plain text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plain_text">plain text</a>. Each line of the file is a data&nbsp;<a title="Record (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Record_(computer_science)">record</a>. Each record consists of one or more&nbsp;<a title="Field (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Field_(computer_science)">fields</a>, separated by&nbsp;<a title="Comma" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comma">commas</a>. The use of the comma as a field separator is the source of the name for this&nbsp;<a title="File format" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File_format">file format</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Compiler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compiler">Compiler</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">computer program</a>&nbsp;that transforms computer code written in one&nbsp;<a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language">programming language</a>&nbsp;(the source language) into another programming language (the target language). Compilers are a type of&nbsp;<a title="Translator (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Translator_(computing)">translator</a>&nbsp;that support digital devices, primarily computers. The name&nbsp;<em>compiler</em>&nbsp;is primarily used for programs that translate&nbsp;<a title="Source code" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Source_code">source code</a>&nbsp;from a&nbsp;<a title="High-level programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High-level_programming_language">high-level programming language</a>&nbsp;to a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Lower level language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lower_level_language">lower level language</a>&nbsp;(e.g.,&nbsp;<a title="Assembly language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assembly_language">assembly language</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Object code" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object_code">object code</a>, or&nbsp;<a title="Machine code" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_code">machine code</a>) to create an&nbsp;<a title="Executable" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executable">executable</a>&nbsp;program.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a class="mw-redirect" title="Compiler theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compiler_theory">Compiler theory</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Computability theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computability_theory">Computability theory</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; also known as&nbsp;<strong>recursion theory</strong>, is a branch of&nbsp;<a title="Mathematical logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_logic">mathematical logic</a>, of&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>, and of the&nbsp;<a title="Theory of computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theory_of_computation">theory of computation</a>&nbsp;that originated in the 1930s with the study of&nbsp;<a title="Computable function" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computable_function">computable functions</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Turing degree" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turing_degree">Turing degrees</a>. The field has since expanded to include the study of generalized computability and definability. In these areas, recursion theory overlaps with&nbsp;<a title="Proof theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proof_theory">proof theory</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Effective descriptive set theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Effective_descriptive_set_theory">effective descriptive set theory</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computation">Computation</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is any type of&nbsp;<a title="Calculation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calculation">calculation</a><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;that includes both arithmetical and non-arithmetical steps and follows a well-defined&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Model (abstract)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Model_(abstract)">model</a>, for example an&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithm</a>. The study of computation is paramount to the discipline of&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Computational biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_biology">Computational biology</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Computational chemistry" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_chemistry">Computational chemistry</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a branch of&nbsp;<a title="Chemistry" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemistry">chemistry</a>&nbsp;that uses&nbsp;<a title="Computer simulation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_simulation">computer simulation</a>&nbsp;to assist in solving chemical problems. It uses methods of&nbsp;<a title="Theoretical chemistry" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theoretical_chemistry">theoretical chemistry</a>, incorporated into efficient&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">computer programs</a>, to calculate the structures and properties of&nbsp;<a title="Molecule" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecule">molecules</a>&nbsp;and solids.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Computational complexity theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_complexity_theory">Computational complexity theory</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; focuses on classifying computational problems according to their inherent difficulty, and relating these classes to each other. A computational problem is a task solved by a computer. A computation problem is solvable by mechanical application of mathematical steps, such as an algorithm.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Computational model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_model">Computational model</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Mathematical model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_model">mathematical model</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Computational science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_science">computational science</a>&nbsp;that requires extensive&nbsp;<a title="Computational resource" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_resource">computational resources</a>&nbsp;to study the behavior of a&nbsp;<a title="Complex system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Complex_system">complex system</a>&nbsp;by&nbsp;<a title="Computer simulation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_simulation">computer simulation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Computational neuroscience" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_neuroscience">Computational neuroscience</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (also known as&nbsp;<strong>theoretical neuroscience</strong>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<strong>mathematical neuroscience</strong>) is a branch of&nbsp;<a title="Neuroscience" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuroscience">neuroscience</a>&nbsp;which employs mathematical models, theoretical analysis and abstractions of the brain to understand the principles that govern the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Developmental neuroscience" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Developmental_neuroscience">development</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Neuroanatomy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuroanatomy">structure</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Neurophysiology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neurophysiology">physiology</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Cognitive neuroscience" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive_neuroscience">cognitive abilities</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="Nervous system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nervous_system">nervous system</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Trappenberg_2002_54-0" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Computational physics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_physics">Computational physics</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Computational science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_science">Computational science</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (also&nbsp;<strong>scientific computing</strong>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<strong>scientific computation</strong>&nbsp;(<strong>SC</strong>)) is a rapidly growing multidisciplinary field that uses advanced computing capabilities to understand and solve complex problems. It is an area of science which spans many disciplines, but at its core it involves the development of models and simulations to understand natural systems.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Computational steering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_steering">Computational steering</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Computer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer">Computer</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a device that can be instructed to carry out sequences of&nbsp;<a title="Arithmetic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arithmetic">arithmetic</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Boolean algebra" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boolean_algebra">logical</a>&nbsp;operations automatically via&nbsp;<a title="Computer programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_programming">computer programming</a>. Modern computers have the ability to follow generalized sets of operations, called&nbsp;<em><a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">programs</a>.</em>&nbsp;These programs enable computers to perform an extremely wide range of tasks.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Computer architecture" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_architecture">Computer architecture</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computer engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_engineering">computer engineering</a>,&nbsp;<strong>computer architecture</strong>&nbsp;is a set of rules and methods that describe the functionality, organization, and implementation of&nbsp;<a title="Computer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer">computer</a>&nbsp;systems. Some definitions of architecture define it as describing the capabilities and programming model of a computer but not a particular implementation.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;In other definitions computer architecture involves&nbsp;<a title="Instruction set architecture" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instruction_set_architecture">instruction set architecture</a>&nbsp;design,&nbsp;<a title="Microarchitecture" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microarchitecture">microarchitecture</a>&nbsp;design,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Logic design" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic_design">logic design</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Implementation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Implementation">implementation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Computer data storage" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_data_storage">Computer data storage</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; often called&nbsp;<strong>storage</strong>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<strong>memory</strong>, is a technology consisting of&nbsp;<a title="Computer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer">computer</a>&nbsp;components and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Data storage device" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_storage_device">recording media</a>&nbsp;that are used to retain digital&nbsp;<a title="Data (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_(computing)">data</a>. It is a core function and fundamental component of computers.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"></sup><sup class="reference">:15&ndash;16</sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Computer ethics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_ethics">Computer ethics</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a part of&nbsp;<a title="Practical philosophy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Practical_philosophy">practical philosophy</a>&nbsp;concerned with how computing professionals should make decisions regarding professional and social conduct.<sup id="cite_ref-BynumVeryShort_61-0" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Computer graphics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_graphics">Computer graphics</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; are pictures and films created using computers. Usually, the term refers to computer-generated image data created with the help of specialized graphical hardware and software. It is a vast and recently developed area of computer science.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Computer network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_network">Computer network</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; or&nbsp;<strong>data network</strong>, is a&nbsp;<a title="Digital signal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_signal">digital</a>&nbsp;<a title="Telecommunications network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telecommunications_network">telecommunications network</a>&nbsp;which allows&nbsp;<a title="Node (networking)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Node_(networking)">nodes</a>&nbsp;to share resources. In computer networks,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computing device" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computing_device">computing devices</a>&nbsp;<a title="Data transmission" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_transmission">exchange data</a>&nbsp;with each other using connections (<a title="Data link" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_link">data links</a>) between nodes. These data links are established over&nbsp;<a title="Networking cables" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Networking_cables">cable media</a>&nbsp;such as wires or optic cables, or&nbsp;<a title="Wireless network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wireless_network">wireless media</a>&nbsp;such as&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="WiFi" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WiFi">WiFi</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Computer programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_programming">Computer programming</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is the process of designing and building an&nbsp;<a title="Executable" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executable">executable</a>&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">computer program</a>&nbsp;for accomplishing a specific&nbsp;<a title="Computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computing">computing</a>&nbsp;task. Programming involves tasks such as analysis, generating&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithms</a>, profiling algorithms' accuracy and resource consumption, and the implementation of algorithms in a chosen&nbsp;<a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language">programming language</a>&nbsp;(commonly referred to as&nbsp;<strong>coding</strong><sup id="cite_ref-tumblr2014_46-1" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tumblr1_47-1" class="reference"></sup>). The&nbsp;<a title="Source code" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Source_code">source code</a>&nbsp;of a program is written in one or more programming languages. The purpose of programming is to find a sequence of instructions that will automate the performance of a task for solving a given problem. The process of programming thus often requires expertise in several different subjects, including knowledge of the&nbsp;<a title="Domain (software engineering)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domain_(software_engineering)">application domain</a>, specialized algorithms, and formal&nbsp;<a title="Logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic">logic</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">Computer science</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is the theory, experimentation, and engineering that form the basis for the design and use of&nbsp;<a title="Computer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer">computers</a>. It involves the study of&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithms</a>&nbsp;that process, store, and communicate&nbsp;<a title="Digital data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_data">digital</a>&nbsp;<a title="Information" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information">information</a>. A&nbsp;<a title="Computer scientist" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_scientist">computer scientist</a>&nbsp;specializes in the theory of computation and the design of computational systems.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Computer scientist" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_scientist">Computer scientist</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Person" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Person">person</a>&nbsp;who has acquired the knowledge of&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>, the study of the theoretical foundations of information and computation and their application.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Computer security" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_security">Computer security</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;&nbsp;<strong>cybersecurity</strong><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<strong>information technology security</strong>&nbsp;(<strong>IT security</strong>) is the protection of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computer system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_system">computer systems</a>&nbsp;from theft or damage to their&nbsp;<a title="Computer hardware" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_hardware">hardware</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software">software</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Data (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_(computing)">electronic data</a>, as well as from&nbsp;<a title="Denial-of-service attack" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denial-of-service_attack">disruption</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Botnet" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Botnet">misdirection</a>&nbsp;of the services they provide.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Computer vision" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_vision">Computer vision</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;is an&nbsp;<a title="Interdisciplinarity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interdisciplinarity">interdisciplinary scientific field</a>&nbsp;that deals with how computers can be made to gain high-level understanding from&nbsp;<a title="Digital image" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_image">digital images</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Video" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Video">videos</a>. From the perspective of&nbsp;<a title="Engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Engineering">engineering</a>, it seeks to automate tasks that the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Human visual system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_visual_system">human visual system</a>&nbsp;can do.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Concatenation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concatenation">Concatenation</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Concurrency (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concurrency_(computer_science)">Concurrency</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; refers to the ability of different parts or units of a program, algorithm, or problem to be executed out-of-order or in partial order, without affecting the final outcome. This allows for parallel execution of the concurrent units, which can significantly improve overall speed of the execution in multi-processor and multi-core systems. In more technical terms, concurrency refers to the decomposability property of a program, algorithm, or problem into order-independent or partially-ordered components or units.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Conditional (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conditional_(computer_programming)">Conditional</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;&nbsp;<strong>Conditional statements</strong>,&nbsp;<strong>conditional expressions</strong>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<strong>conditional constructs</strong>&nbsp;are features of a&nbsp;<a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language">programming language</a>, which perform different computations or actions depending on whether a programmer-specified&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Boolean datatype" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boolean_datatype">boolean</a>&nbsp;<em>condition</em>&nbsp;evaluates to true or false. Apart from the case of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Branch predication" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Branch_predication">branch predication</a>, this is always achieved by selectively altering the&nbsp;<a title="Control flow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_flow">control flow</a>&nbsp;based on some condition.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Continuation-passing style" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continuation-passing_style">Continuation-passing style</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Functional programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Functional_programming">functional programming</a>,&nbsp;<strong>continuation-passing style</strong>&nbsp;(<strong>CPS</strong>) is a style of programming in which&nbsp;<a title="Control flow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_flow">control</a>&nbsp;is passed explicitly in the form of a&nbsp;<a title="Continuation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continuation">continuation</a>. This is contrasted with&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Direct style" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct_style">direct style</a>, which is the usual style of programming.&nbsp;<a title="Gerald Jay Sussman" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gerald_Jay_Sussman">Gerald Jay Sussman</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Guy L. Steele, Jr." href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guy_L._Steele,_Jr.">Guy L. Steele, Jr.</a>&nbsp;coined the phrase in&nbsp;<a title="AI Memo" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AI_Memo">AI Memo</a>&nbsp;349 (1975), which sets out the first version of the&nbsp;<a title="Scheme (programming language)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scheme_(programming_language)">Scheme</a>&nbsp;programming language.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Control flow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_flow">Control flow</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (or&nbsp;<strong>flow of control</strong>) is the order in which individual&nbsp;<a title="Statement (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statement_(computer_science)">statements</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Instruction (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instruction_(computer_science)">instructions</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Function call" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Function_call">function calls</a>&nbsp;of an&nbsp;<a title="Imperative programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperative_programming">imperative</a>&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">program</a>&nbsp;are&nbsp;<a title="Execution (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Execution_(computing)">executed</a>&nbsp;or evaluated. The emphasis on explicit control flow distinguishes an&nbsp;<em><a title="Imperative programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperative_programming">imperative programming</a></em>&nbsp;language from a&nbsp;<em><a title="Declarative programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Declarative_programming">declarative programming</a></em>&nbsp;language.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Creative Commons" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Creative_Commons">Creative Commons</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (CC), is an American&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Non-profit organization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-profit_organization">non-profit organization</a>&nbsp;devoted to expanding the range of&nbsp;<a title="Creativity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Creativity">creative</a>&nbsp;works available for others to build upon legally and to share.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;The organization has released several&nbsp;<a title="Copyright" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copyright">copyright</a>-<a title="License" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/License">licenses</a>, known as&nbsp;<a title="Creative Commons license" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Creative_Commons_license">Creative Commons licenses</a>, free of charge to the public.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Cryptography" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptography">Cryptography</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Comma-separated values" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comma-separated_values">CSV</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; comma-separated values.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Cyberbullying" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyberbullying">Cyberbullying</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; or cyberharassment, is a form of&nbsp;<a title="Bullying" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bullying">bullying</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Harassment" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harassment">harassment</a>&nbsp;using electronic means. Cyberbullying and cyberharassment are also known as online bullying.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Cyberspace" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyberspace">Cyberspace</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is widespread, interconnected digital&nbsp;<a title="Technology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technology">technology</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="D" class="mw-headline">D</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><strong><a title="Data center" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_center">Data center</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; or&nbsp;<strong>data centre</strong>, is a dedicated space used to house&nbsp;<a title="Computer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer">computer systems</a>&nbsp;and associated components, such as&nbsp;<a title="Telecommunication" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telecommunication">telecommunications</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Computer data storage" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_data_storage">storage systems</a>. It generally includes&nbsp;<a title="Redundancy (engineering)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Redundancy_(engineering)">redundant</a>&nbsp;or backup components and infrastructure for&nbsp;<a title="Power supply" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Power_supply">power supply</a>, data communications connections, environmental controls (e.g. air conditioning, fire suppression) and various security devices.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT92212_72-0" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceDC2_73-0" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Database" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Database">Database</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is an organized collection of&nbsp;<a title="Data (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_(computing)">data</a>, generally stored and accessed electronically from a computer system. Where databases are more complex they are often developed using formal&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_computer_science#Design_and_modeling">design and modeling</a>&nbsp;techniques.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Data mining" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_mining">Data mining</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Data science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_science">Data science</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Interdisciplinary" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interdisciplinary">interdisciplinary</a>&nbsp;field that uses scientific methods, processes, algorithms and systems to extract&nbsp;<a title="Knowledge" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge">knowledge</a>&nbsp;and insights from&nbsp;<a title="Data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data">data</a>&nbsp;in various forms, both structured and unstructured,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;similar to&nbsp;<a title="Data mining" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_mining">data mining</a>. Data science is a "concept to unify statistics, data analysis, machine learning and their related methods" in order to "understand and analyze actual phenomena" with data.<sup id="cite_ref-Hayashi_76-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;It employs techniques and theories drawn from many fields within the context of&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Statistics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistics">statistics</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Information science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_science">information science</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Data structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_structure">Data structure</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a data organization, management and storage format that enables&nbsp;<a title="Algorithmic efficiency" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithmic_efficiency">efficient</a>&nbsp;access and modification.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;More precisely, a data structure is a collection of data values, the relationships among them, and the functions or operations that can be applied to the data.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Data type" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_type">Data type</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; or simply&nbsp;<strong>type</strong>&nbsp;is an attribute of&nbsp;<a title="Data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data">data</a>&nbsp;which tells the&nbsp;<a title="Compiler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compiler">compiler</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Interpreter (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interpreter_(computing)">interpreter</a>&nbsp;how the programmer intends to use the data. Most programming languages support common data types of&nbsp;<a title="Real number" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_number">real</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Integer (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Integer_(computer_science)">integer</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Boolean data type" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boolean_data_type">boolean</a>. A data type constrains the values that an&nbsp;<a title="Expression (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expression_(computer_science)">expression</a>, such as a variable or a function, might take. This data type defines the operations that can be done on the data, the meaning of the data, and the way values of that type can be stored. A type of value from which an expression may take its value.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Debugging" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Debugging">Debugging</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is the process of finding and resolving defects or problems within a computer program that prevent correct operation of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computer software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_software">computer software</a>&nbsp;or a&nbsp;<a title="System" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/System">system</a>. Debugging tactics can involve&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Interactive" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interactive">interactive</a>&nbsp;debugging,&nbsp;<a title="Control flow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_flow">control flow</a>&nbsp;analysis,&nbsp;<a title="Unit testing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unit_testing">unit testing</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Integration testing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Integration_testing">integration testing</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Logfile" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logfile">log file analysis</a>, monitoring at the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Application monitoring" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_monitoring">application</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="System monitoring" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/System_monitoring">system</a>&nbsp;level,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Memory dump" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Memory_dump">memory dumps</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Profiling (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Profiling_(computer_programming)">profiling</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Declaration (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Declaration_(computer_programming)">Declaration</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computer programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_programming">computer programming</a>, a&nbsp;<strong>declaration</strong>&nbsp;is a&nbsp;<a title="Language construct" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Language_construct">language construct</a>&nbsp;that specifies properties of an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Identifier (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Identifier_(computer_programming)">identifier</a>: it declares what a word (identifier) "means".<sup id="cite_ref-c11_83-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;Declarations are most commonly used for&nbsp;<a title="Subroutine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subroutine">functions</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Variable (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variable_(computer_science)">variables</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Constant (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constant_(computer_programming)">constants</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Class (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_(computer_programming)">classes</a>, but can also be used for other entities such as enumerations and type definitions.<sup id="cite_ref-c11_83-1" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;Beyond the name (the identifier itself) and the kind of entity (function, variable, etc.), declarations typically specify the&nbsp;<a title="Data type" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_type">data type</a>&nbsp;(for variables and constants), or the&nbsp;<a title="Type signature" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Type_signature">type signature</a>&nbsp;(for functions); types may also include dimensions, such as for arrays. A declaration is used to announce the existence of the entity to the&nbsp;<a title="Compiler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compiler">compiler</a>; this is important in those&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Strongly typed" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strongly_typed">strongly typed</a>&nbsp;languages that require functions, variables, and constants, and their types to be specified with a declaration before use, and is used in&nbsp;<a title="Forward declaration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forward_declaration">forward declaration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;The term "declaration" is frequently contrasted with the term "definition",<sup id="cite_ref-c11_83-2" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;but meaning and usage varies significantly between languages.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Digital data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_data">Digital data</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; in&nbsp;<a title="Information theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_theory">information theory</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Information systems" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_systems">information systems</a>, is the discrete, discontinuous&nbsp;<a title="Representation (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Representation_(mathematics)">representation</a>&nbsp;of information or works.&nbsp;<a title="Number" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Number">Numbers</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Letter (alphabet)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Letter_(alphabet)">letters</a>&nbsp;are commonly used representations.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Digital signal processing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_signal_processing">Digital signal processing</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (<strong>DSP</strong>) is the use of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Digital processing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_processing">digital processing</a>, such as by computers or more specialized&nbsp;<a title="Digital signal processor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_signal_processor">digital signal processors</a>, to perform a wide variety of&nbsp;<a title="Signal processing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Signal_processing">signal processing</a>&nbsp;operations. The signals processed in this manner are a sequence of numbers that represent&nbsp;<a title="Sampling (signal processing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sampling_(signal_processing)">samples</a>&nbsp;of a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Continuous variable" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continuous_variable">continuous variable</a>&nbsp;in a domain such as time, space, or frequency.</li>
<li><strong><a class="mw-redirect" title="Discrete event simulation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discrete_event_simulation">Discrete event simulation</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (<strong>DES</strong>) models the operation of a&nbsp;<a title="System" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/System">system</a>&nbsp;as a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Discrete time" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discrete_time">discrete</a>&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Sequence of events" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sequence_of_events">sequence of events</a>&nbsp;in time. Each event occurs at a particular instant in time and marks a change of&nbsp;<a title="State (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_(computer_science)">state</a>&nbsp;in the system.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;Between consecutive events, no change in the system is assumed to occur; thus the&nbsp;<a title="Simulation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simulation">simulation</a>&nbsp;can directly jump in time from one event to the next.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Disk storage" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disk_storage">Disk storage</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Distributed computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Distributed_computing">Distributed computing</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a field of&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>&nbsp;that studies distributed systems. A&nbsp;<em>distributed system</em>&nbsp;is a system whose components are located on different&nbsp;<a title="Computer network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_network">networked computers</a>, which communicate and coordinate their actions by&nbsp;<a title="Message passing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Message_passing">passing messages</a>&nbsp;to one another.<sup id="cite_ref-Coulouris_86-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;The components interact with one another in order to achieve a common goal. Three significant characteristics of distributed systems are: concurrency of components,&nbsp;<a title="Clock synchronization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clock_synchronization">lack of a global clock</a>, and independent failure of components.<sup id="cite_ref-Coulouris_86-1" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;Examples of distributed systems vary from&nbsp;<a title="Service-oriented architecture" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Service-oriented_architecture">SOA-based systems</a>&nbsp;to&nbsp;<a title="Massively multiplayer online game" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Massively_multiplayer_online_game">massively multiplayer online games</a>&nbsp;to&nbsp;<a title="Peer-to-peer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peer-to-peer">peer-to-peer applications</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a class="mw-redirect" title="Divide and conquer algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Divide_and_conquer_algorithm">Divide and conquer algorithm</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Algorithm design paradigm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm_design_paradigm">algorithm design paradigm</a>&nbsp;based on multi-branched&nbsp;<a title="Recursion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recursion">recursion</a>. A divide-and-conquer&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithm</a>&nbsp;works by recursively breaking down a problem into two or more sub-problems of the same or related type, until these become simple enough to be solved directly. The solutions to the sub-problems are then combined to give a solution to the original problem.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Domain Name System" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domain_Name_System">DNS</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; see&nbsp;<em><strong>Domain Name System</strong></em>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Software documentation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_documentation">Documentation</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;&nbsp;<strong>Software documentation</strong>&nbsp;is written text or illustration that accompanies&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computer software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_software">computer software</a>&nbsp;or is embedded in the source code. It either explains how it operates or how to use it, and may mean different things to people in different roles.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Domain Name System" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domain_Name_System">Domain Name System</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (<strong>DNS</strong>) is a&nbsp;<a title="Hierarchy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hierarchy">hierarchical</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Decentralised system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decentralised_system">decentralized</a>&nbsp;naming system for computers, services, or other resources connected to the&nbsp;<a title="Internet" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet">Internet</a>&nbsp;or a private network. It associates various information with&nbsp;<a title="Domain name" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domain_name">domain names</a>&nbsp;assigned to each of the participating entities. Most prominently, it translates more readily memorized domain names to the numerical&nbsp;<a title="IP address" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IP_address">IP addresses</a>&nbsp;needed for locating and identifying computer services and devices with the underlying&nbsp;<a title="Communication protocol" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communication_protocol">network protocols</a>. By providing a worldwide,&nbsp;<a title="Distributed computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Distributed_computing">distributed</a>&nbsp;<a title="Directory service" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Directory_service">directory service</a>, the Domain Name System has been an essential component of the functionality of the Internet since 1985.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Double-precision floating-point format" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Double-precision_floating-point_format">Double-precision floating-point format</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Computer number format" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_number_format">computer number format</a>. It represents a wide&nbsp;<a title="Dynamic range" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dynamic_range">dynamic range</a>&nbsp;of numeric values by using a floating radix point.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Download" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Download">Download</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computer network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_network">computer networks</a>,&nbsp;<strong>download</strong>&nbsp;means to receive data from a remote system, typically a&nbsp;<a title="Server (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Server_(computing)">server</a><sup id="cite_ref-main_87-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;such as a&nbsp;<a title="Web server" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_server">web server</a>, an&nbsp;<a title="File Transfer Protocol" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File_Transfer_Protocol">FTP</a>&nbsp;server, an&nbsp;<a title="Email" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Email">email</a>&nbsp;server, or other similar systems. This contrasts with&nbsp;<a title="Upload" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Upload">uploading</a>, where data is sent&nbsp;<em>to</em>&nbsp;a remote server. A&nbsp;<em>download</em>&nbsp;is a&nbsp;<a title="Computer file" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_file">file</a>&nbsp;offered for downloading or that has been downloaded, or the process of receiving such a file.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="E" class="mw-headline">E</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><strong><a title="Edge device" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edge_device">Edge device</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a device which provides an entry point into enterprise or service provider core networks. Examples include&nbsp;<a title="Router (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Router_(computing)">routers</a>, routing&nbsp;<a title="Network switch" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Network_switch">switches</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Integrated access device" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Integrated_access_device">integrated access devices</a>&nbsp;(IADs), multiplexers, and a variety of&nbsp;<a title="Metropolitan area network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metropolitan_area_network">metropolitan area network</a>&nbsp;(MAN) and&nbsp;<a title="Wide area network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wide_area_network">wide area network</a>&nbsp;(WAN) access devices. Edge devices also provide connections into carrier and service provider networks. An edge device that connects a&nbsp;<a title="Local area network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Local_area_network">local area network</a>&nbsp;to a high speed switch or backbone (such as an ATM switch) may be called an edge concentrator.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Encryption" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Encryption">Encryption</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Event (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Event_(computing)">Event</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; Is an action or occurrence recognized by software, often originating&nbsp;<a title="Asynchronous I/O" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asynchronous_I/O">asynchronously</a>&nbsp;from the external environment, that may be&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Event handler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Event_handler">handled</a>&nbsp;by the software. Because an event is an entity which encapsulates the action and the contextual variables triggering the action we can use the&nbsp;<a title="Acrostic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acrostic">acrostic</a>&nbsp;<a title="Mnemonic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mnemonic">mnemonic</a>&nbsp;of an event as an "<strong>E</strong>xecution&nbsp;<strong>V</strong>ariable&nbsp;<strong>E</strong>ncapsulating&nbsp;<strong>N</strong>amed&nbsp;<strong>T</strong>rigger" to clarify the concept.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Event-driven programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Event-driven_programming">Event-driven programming</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Programming paradigm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_paradigm">programming paradigm</a>&nbsp;in which the&nbsp;<a title="Control flow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_flow">flow of the program</a>&nbsp;is determined by&nbsp;<a title="Event (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Event_(computing)">events</a>&nbsp;such as user actions (<a title="Computer mouse" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_mouse">mouse</a>&nbsp;clicks, key presses),&nbsp;<a title="Sensor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sensor">sensor</a>&nbsp;outputs, or&nbsp;<a title="Message passing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Message_passing">messages</a>&nbsp;from other programs or&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Thread (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thread_(computer_science)">threads</a>. Event-driven programming is the dominant paradigm used in&nbsp;<a title="Graphical user interface" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graphical_user_interface">graphical user interfaces</a>&nbsp;and other applications (e.g., JavaScript&nbsp;<a title="Web application" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_application">web applications</a>) that are centered on performing certain actions in response to&nbsp;<a title="Input/output" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Input/output">user input</a>. This is also true of programming for&nbsp;<a title="Device driver" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Device_driver">device drivers</a>&nbsp;(e.g.,&nbsp;<a title="P (programming language)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/P_(programming_language)">P</a>&nbsp;in USB device driver stacks<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"></sup>).</li>
<li><strong><a class="mw-redirect" title="Evolutionary computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_computing">Evolutionary computing</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a family of&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithms</a>&nbsp;for&nbsp;<a title="Global optimization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_optimization">global optimization</a>&nbsp;inspired by&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Biological evolution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological_evolution">biological evolution</a>, and the subfield of&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="new" title="Soft computing (page does not exist)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Soft_computing&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1">soft computing</a>&nbsp;studying these algorithms. In technical terms, they are a family of population-based&nbsp;<a title="Trial and error" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trial_and_error">trial and error</a>&nbsp;problem solvers with a&nbsp;<a title="Metaheuristic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metaheuristic">metaheuristic</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Stochastic optimization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stochastic_optimization">stochastic optimization</a>&nbsp;character.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Executable" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executable">Executable</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;&nbsp;<strong>executable code</strong>&nbsp;or an&nbsp;<strong>executable file</strong>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<strong>executable program</strong>, sometimes simply referred to as an&nbsp;<strong>executable</strong>, causes a computer "to perform indicated tasks according to encoded&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Instruction (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instruction_(computer_science)">instructions</a>,"<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;as opposed to a&nbsp;<a title="Data (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_(computing)">data file</a>&nbsp;that must be&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Parser" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parser">parsed</a>&nbsp;by a program to be meaningful. The exact interpretation depends upon the use - while "instructions" is traditionally taken to mean&nbsp;<a title="Machine code" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_code">machine code</a>&nbsp;instructions for a physical&nbsp;<a title="Central processing unit" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_processing_unit">CPU</a>, in some contexts a file containing&nbsp;<a title="Bytecode" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bytecode">bytecode</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Scripting language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scripting_language">scripting language</a>&nbsp;instructions may also be considered executable.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Exception handling" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exception_handling">Exception handling</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is the process of responding to the occurrence, during&nbsp;<a title="Computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computation">computation</a>, of&nbsp;<em>exceptions</em>&nbsp;&ndash; anomalous or exceptional conditions requiring special processing &ndash; often disrupting the normal flow of&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">program</a>&nbsp;<a title="Execution (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Execution_(computing)">execution</a>. It is provided by specialized&nbsp;<a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language">programming language</a>&nbsp;constructs,&nbsp;<a title="Computer hardware" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_hardware">computer hardware</a>&nbsp;mechanisms like&nbsp;<a title="Interrupt" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interrupt">interrupts</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Operating system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operating_system">operating system</a>&nbsp;<a title="Inter-process communication" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inter-process_communication">IPC</a>&nbsp;facilities like&nbsp;<a title="Signal (IPC)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Signal_(IPC)">signals</a>.</li>
<li><strong>Executable module</strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Expression (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expression_(computer_science)">Expression</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; An expression in a&nbsp;<a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language">programming language</a>&nbsp;is a combination of one or more&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Constant (programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constant_(programming)">constants</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Variable (programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variable_(programming)">variables</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Operator (programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operator_(programming)">operators</a>, and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Function (programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Function_(programming)">functions</a>&nbsp;that the programming language interprets (according to its particular&nbsp;<a title="Order of operations" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Order_of_operations">rules of precedence</a>&nbsp;and of association) and computes to produce ("to return", in a&nbsp;<a title="State (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_(computer_science)">stateful</a>&nbsp;environment) another value. This process, as for&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Mathematical expression" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_expression">mathematical expressions</a>, is called evaluation.</li>
<li><strong>External library</strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="F" class="mw-headline">F</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><strong><a class="mw-redirect" title="Fault-tolerant computer system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fault-tolerant_computer_system">Fault-tolerant computer system</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; are systems designed around the concepts of&nbsp;<a title="Fault tolerance" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fault_tolerance">fault tolerance</a>. In essence, they must be able to continue working to a level of satisfaction in the presence of errors or breakdowns.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Feasibility study" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feasibility_study">Feasibility study</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; aims to objectively and rationally uncover the strengths and weaknesses of an existing business or proposed venture, opportunities and threats present in the&nbsp;<a title="Natural environment" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_environment">natural environment</a>, the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Resources" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resources">resources</a>&nbsp;required to carry through, and ultimately the prospects for success.<sup id="cite_ref-Justis_90-0" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;In its simplest terms, the two criteria to judge feasibility are&nbsp;<a title="Cost" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cost">cost</a>&nbsp;required and&nbsp;<a title="Value (economics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Value_(economics)">value</a>&nbsp;to be attained.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Filename extension" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Filename_extension">Filename extension</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is an identifier specified as a&nbsp;<a title="Substring" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Substring">suffix</a>&nbsp;to the&nbsp;<a title="Filename" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Filename">name</a>&nbsp;of a&nbsp;<a title="Computer file" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_file">computer file</a>. The extension indicates a characteristic of the file contents or its intended use.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Filter (software)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Filter_(software)">Filter (software)</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">computer program</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Subroutine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subroutine">subroutine</a>&nbsp;to process a&nbsp;<a title="Stream (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stream_(computing)">stream</a>, producing another stream. While a single filter can be used individually, they are frequently strung together to form a&nbsp;<a title="Pipeline (software)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pipeline_(software)">pipeline</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a class="mw-redirect" title="Floating point arithmetic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Floating_point_arithmetic">Floating point arithmetic</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="For loop" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/For_loop">For loop</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; A for-loop (or simply for loop) is a&nbsp;<a title="Control flow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_flow">control flow</a>&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Statement (programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statement_(programming)">statement</a>&nbsp;for specifying&nbsp;<a title="Iteration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iteration">iteration</a>, which allows code to be&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Execution (computers)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Execution_(computers)">executed</a>&nbsp;repeatedly. Various keywords are used to specify this statement: descendants of&nbsp;<a title="ALGOL" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ALGOL">ALGOL</a>&nbsp;use "for", while descendants of&nbsp;<a title="Fortran" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fortran">Fortran</a>&nbsp;use "do". There are other possibilities, for example&nbsp;<a title="COBOL" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COBOL">COBOL</a>&nbsp;which uses "PERFORM VARYING".</li>
<li><strong><a title="Formal methods" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_methods">Formal methods</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; are a particular kind of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Mathematically" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematically">mathematically</a>&nbsp;based technique for the&nbsp;<a title="Formal specification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_specification">specification</a>, development and&nbsp;<a title="Formal verification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_verification">verification</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software">software</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Computer hardware" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_hardware">hardware</a>&nbsp;systems.<sup id="cite_ref-butler_93-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;The use of formal methods for software and hardware design is motivated by the expectation that, as in other engineering disciplines, performing appropriate mathematical analysis can contribute to the reliability and robustness of a design.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Formal verification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_verification">Formal verification</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is the act of&nbsp;<a title="Mathematical proof" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_proof">proving</a>&nbsp;or disproving the&nbsp;<a title="Correctness (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Correctness_(computer_science)">correctness</a>&nbsp;of intended&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Algorithms" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithms">algorithms</a>&nbsp;underlying a system with respect to a certain&nbsp;<a title="Formal specification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_specification">formal specification</a>&nbsp;or property, using&nbsp;<a title="Formal methods" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_methods">formal methods</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Functional programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Functional_programming">Functional programming</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Programming paradigm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_paradigm">programming paradigm</a>&mdash;a style of building the structure and elements of&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">computer programs</a>&mdash;that treats&nbsp;<a title="Computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computation">computation</a>&nbsp;as the evaluation of&nbsp;<a title="Function (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Function_(mathematics)">mathematical functions</a>&nbsp;and avoids changing-<a class="mw-redirect" title="Program state" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Program_state">state</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Immutable object" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immutable_object">mutable</a>&nbsp;data. It is a&nbsp;<a title="Declarative programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Declarative_programming">declarative programming</a>&nbsp;paradigm in that programming is done with&nbsp;<a title="Expression (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expression_(computer_science)">expressions</a>&nbsp;or declarations<sup id="cite_ref-expression_style_96-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;instead of&nbsp;<a title="Statement (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statement_(computer_science)">statements</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="G" class="mw-headline">G</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><strong><a title="Game theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Game_theory">Game theory</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is the study of&nbsp;<a title="Mathematical model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_model">mathematical models</a>&nbsp;of strategic interaction between rational decision-makers.<sup id="cite_ref-Myerson_97-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;It has applications in all fields of&nbsp;<a title="Social science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_science">social science</a>, as well as in&nbsp;<a title="Logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic">logic</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>. Originally, it addressed&nbsp;<a title="Zero-sum game" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zero-sum_game">zero-sum games</a>, in which each participant's gains or losses are exactly balanced by those of the other participants. Today, game theory applies to a wide range of behavioral relations, and is now an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Umbrella term" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umbrella_term">umbrella term</a>&nbsp;for the&nbsp;<a title="Science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science">science</a>&nbsp;of logical decision making in humans, animals, and computers.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Garbage in, garbage out" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Garbage_in,_garbage_out">Garbage in, garbage out</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (GIGO), describes the concept that flawed, or nonsense&nbsp;<a title="Input (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Input_(computer_science)">input</a>&nbsp;data produces nonsense&nbsp;<a title="Input/output" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Input/output">output</a>&nbsp;or "garbage".</li>
<li><strong><a title="GIF" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GIF">GIF</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; Graphics Interchange Format.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Gigabyte" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gigabyte">Gigabyte</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a multiple of the unit&nbsp;<a title="Byte" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byte">byte</a>&nbsp;for digital information. The&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="SI prefix" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SI_prefix">prefix</a>&nbsp;<em><a title="Giga-" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giga-">giga</a></em>&nbsp;means 10<sup>9</sup>&nbsp;in the&nbsp;<a title="International System of Units" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_System_of_Units">International System of Units</a>&nbsp;(SI). Therefore, one gigabyte is&nbsp;1000000000bytes. The unit symbol for the gigabyte is GB.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Global variable" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_variable">Global variable</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computer programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_programming">computer programming</a>, a global variable is a variable with global&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Scope (programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scope_(programming)">scope</a>, meaning that it is visible (hence accessible) throughout the program, unless&nbsp;<a title="Variable shadowing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variable_shadowing">shadowed</a>. The set of all global variables is known as the&nbsp;<em>global environment</em>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<em>global state.</em>&nbsp;In compiled languages, global variables are generally&nbsp;<a title="Static variable" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Static_variable">static variables</a>, whose&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Variable (programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variable_(programming)#Scope_and_extent">extent</a>&nbsp;(lifetime) is the entire runtime of the program, though in interpreted languages (including&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Command-line interpreter" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Command-line_interpreter">command-line interpreters</a>), global variables are generally dynamically allocated when declared, since they are not known ahead of time.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Graph theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graph_theory">Graph theory</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>, graph theory is the study of&nbsp;<em><a title="Graph (discrete mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graph_(discrete_mathematics)">graphs</a></em>, which are mathematical structures used to model pairwise relations between objects. A graph in this context is made up of&nbsp;<em><a title="Vertex (graph theory)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vertex_(graph_theory)">vertices</a></em>&nbsp;(also called&nbsp;<em>nodes</em>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<em>points</em>) which are connected by&nbsp;<em><a title="Glossary of graph theory terms" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_graph_theory_terms#edge">edges</a></em>&nbsp;(also called&nbsp;<em>links</em>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<em>lines</em>). A distinction is made between undirected graphs, where edges link two vertices symmetrically, and directed graphs, where edges link two vertices asymmetrically.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="H" class="mw-headline">H</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><strong><a title="Computational complexity theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_complexity_theory">Hard problem</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; Computational complexity theory focuses on classifying computational problems according to their inherent difficulty, and relating these classes to each other. A computational problem is a task solved by a computer. A computation problem is solvable by mechanical application of mathematical steps, such as an algorithm.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Hash function" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hash_function">Hash function</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is any&nbsp;<a title="Function (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Function_(mathematics)">function</a>&nbsp;that can be used to map&nbsp;<a title="Data (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_(computing)">data</a>&nbsp;of arbitrary size to data of a fixed size. The values returned by a hash function are called&nbsp;<strong>hash values</strong>,&nbsp;<strong>hash codes</strong>,&nbsp;<strong>digests</strong>, or simply&nbsp;<strong>hashes</strong>. Hash functions are often used in combination with a&nbsp;<a title="Hash table" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hash_table">hash table</a>, a common&nbsp;<a title="Data structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_structure">data structure</a>&nbsp;used in computer software for rapid data lookup. Hash functions accelerate table or database lookup by detecting duplicated records in a large file.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Hash table" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hash_table">Hash table</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computing">computing</a>, a&nbsp;<strong>hash table</strong>&nbsp;(<strong>hash map</strong>) is a&nbsp;<a title="Data structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_structure">data structure</a>&nbsp;that implements an&nbsp;<a title="Associative array" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Associative_array">associative array</a>&nbsp;<a title="Abstract data type" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abstract_data_type">abstract data type</a>, a structure that can map&nbsp;<a title="Unique key" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unique_key">keys</a>&nbsp;to&nbsp;<a title="Value (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Value_(computer_science)">values</a>. A hash table uses a&nbsp;<a title="Hash function" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hash_function">hash function</a>&nbsp;to compute an&nbsp;<em>index</em>&nbsp;into an array of&nbsp;<em>buckets</em>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<em>slots</em>, from which the desired value can be found.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Heap (data structure)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heap_(data_structure)">Heap</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a specialized&nbsp;<a title="Tree (data structure)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tree_(data_structure)">tree</a>-based&nbsp;<a title="Data structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_structure">data structure</a>&nbsp;which is essentially an almost complete<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;tree that satisfies the&nbsp;<em>heap property:</em>&nbsp;if P is a parent&nbsp;<a title="Node (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Node_(computer_science)">node</a>&nbsp;of C, then the&nbsp;<em>key</em>&nbsp;(the&nbsp;<em>value</em>) of P is either greater than or equal to (in a&nbsp;<em>max heap</em>) or less than or equal to (in a&nbsp;<em>min heap</em>) the key of C.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;The node at the "top" of the heap (with no parents) is called the&nbsp;<em>root</em>&nbsp;node.</li>
