<li><strong><a title="Heapsort" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heapsort">Heapsort</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Comparison sort" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comparison_sort">comparison-based</a>&nbsp;<a title="Sorting algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sorting_algorithm">sorting algorithm</a>. Heapsort can be thought of as an improved&nbsp;<a title="Selection sort" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Selection_sort">selection sort</a>: like that algorithm, it divides its input into a sorted and an unsorted region, and it iteratively shrinks the unsorted region by extracting the largest element and moving that to the sorted region. The improvement consists of the use of a&nbsp;<a title="Heap (data structure)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heap_(data_structure)">heap</a>&nbsp;data structure rather than a linear-time search to find the maximum.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a class="mw-redirect" title="Human-computer interaction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human-computer_interaction">Human-computer interaction</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (<strong>HCI</strong>) researches the design and use of computer technology, focused on the interfaces between people (<a title="User (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/User_(computing)">users</a>) and computers. Researchers in the field of HCI both observe the ways in which humans interact with computers and design technologies that let humans interact with computers in novel ways. As a field of research, human&ndash;computer interaction is situated at the intersection of&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Behavioral sciences" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Behavioral_sciences">behavioral sciences</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Design" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Design">design</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Media studies" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Media_studies">media studies</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Outline of human&ndash;computer interaction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Outline_of_human%E2%80%93computer_interaction#Related_fields">several other fields of study</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="I" class="mw-headline">I</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><strong><a title="Integrated development environment" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Integrated_development_environment">IDE</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; integrated development environment.</li>
<li><strong><a class="mw-redirect" title="Image processing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Image_processing">Image processing</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Imperative programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperative_programming">Imperative programming</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Programming paradigm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_paradigm">programming paradigm</a>&nbsp;that uses&nbsp;<a title="Statement (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statement_(computer_science)">statements</a>&nbsp;that change a program's&nbsp;<a title="State (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_(computer_science)">state</a>. In much the same way that the&nbsp;<a title="Imperative mood" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperative_mood">imperative mood</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Natural language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language">natural languages</a>&nbsp;expresses commands, an imperative program consists of&nbsp;<a title="Command (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Command_(computing)">commands</a>&nbsp;for the computer to perform. Imperative programming focuses on describing&nbsp;<em>how</em>&nbsp;a program operates.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Incremental build model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Incremental_build_model">Incremental build model</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a method of&nbsp;<a title="Software development" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_development">software development</a>&nbsp;where the product is&nbsp;<a title="Software design" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_design">designed</a>, implemented and&nbsp;<a title="Software testing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_testing">tested</a>&nbsp;incrementally (a little more is added each time) until the product is finished. It involves both development and maintenance. The product is defined as finished when it satisfies all of its requirements. This model combines the elements of the&nbsp;<a title="Waterfall model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Waterfall_model">waterfall model</a>&nbsp;with the iterative philosophy of&nbsp;<a title="Software prototyping" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_prototyping">prototyping</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Information space analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_space_analysis">Information space analysis</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Deterministic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deterministic">deterministic</a>&nbsp;method, enhanced by&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">machine intelligence</a>, for locating and assessing&nbsp;<a title="Resource" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resource">resources</a>&nbsp;for team-centric efforts.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Information visualization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_visualization">Information visualization</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a class="mw-redirect" title="Inheritance (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inheritance_(computer_science)">Inheritance</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Object-oriented programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object-oriented_programming">object-oriented programming</a>, inheritance is the mechanism of basing an&nbsp;<a title="Object (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object_(computer_science)">object</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Class (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_(computer_programming)">class</a>&nbsp;upon another object (<a title="Prototype-based programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prototype-based_programming">prototype-based inheritance</a>) or class (<a title="Class-based programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class-based_programming">class-based inheritance</a>), retaining similar implementation. Also defined as deriving new classes (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_computer_science#Subclasses_and_superclasses">sub classes</a>) from existing ones (super class or&nbsp;<a title="Fragile base class" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fragile_base_class">base class</a>) and forming them into a hierarchy of classes.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Input/output" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Input/output">Input/output</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; or I/O (or, informally, io or IO), is the communication between an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Information processing system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_processing_system">information processing system</a>, such as a&nbsp;<a title="Computer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer">computer</a>, and the outside world, possibly a human or another&nbsp;<a title="Information processor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_processor">information processing system</a>.&nbsp;<a title="Information" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information">Inputs</a>&nbsp;are the signals or data received by the system and outputs are the signals or&nbsp;<a title="Data (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_(computing)">data</a>&nbsp;sent from it. The term can also be used as part of an action; to "perform I/O" is to perform an&nbsp;<a title="I/O scheduling" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/I/O_scheduling">input or output operation</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Insertion sort" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Insertion_sort">Insertion sort</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a simple&nbsp;<a title="Sorting algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sorting_algorithm">sorting algorithm</a>&nbsp;that builds the final&nbsp;<a title="Sorted array" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sorted_array">sorted array</a>&nbsp;(or list) one item at a time.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Instruction cycle" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instruction_cycle">Instruction cycle</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (also known as the fetch&ndash;decode&ndash;execute cycle or simply the fetch-execute cycle), is the cycle which the&nbsp;<a title="Central processing unit" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_processing_unit">central processing unit</a>&nbsp;(CPU) follows from&nbsp;<a title="Booting" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Booting">boot-up</a>&nbsp;until the computer has shut down in order to process instructions. It is composed of three main stages: the fetch stage, the decode stage, and the execute stage.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Integer (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Integer_(computer_science)">Integer</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data">datum</a>&nbsp;of integral data type, a&nbsp;<a title="Data type" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_type">data type</a>&nbsp;that represents some&nbsp;<a title="Interval (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interval_(mathematics)">range</a>&nbsp;of mathematical&nbsp;<a title="Integer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Integer">integers</a>. Integral data types may be of different sizes and may or may not be allowed to contain negative values. Integers are commonly represented in a computer as a group of binary digits (bits). The size of the grouping varies so the set of integer sizes available varies between different types of computers. Computer hardware, including&nbsp;<a title="Virtual machine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virtual_machine">virtual machines</a>, nearly always provide a way to represent a processor&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Word size" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Word_size">register</a>&nbsp;or memory address as an integer.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Integrated development environment" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Integrated_development_environment">Integrated development environment</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (IDE), is a&nbsp;<a title="Application software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_software">software application</a>&nbsp;that provides comprehensive facilities to&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computer programmer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_programmer">computer programmers</a>&nbsp;for&nbsp;<a title="Software development" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_development">software development</a>. An IDE normally consists of at least a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Source code editor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Source_code_editor">source code editor</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Build automation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Build_automation">build automation</a>&nbsp;tools, and a&nbsp;<a title="Debugger" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Debugger">debugger</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Integration testing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Integration_testing">Integration testing</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (sometimes called integration and testing, abbreviated I&amp;T) is the phase in&nbsp;<a title="Software testing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_testing">software testing</a>&nbsp;in which individual software modules are combined and tested as a group. Integration testing is conducted to evaluate the&nbsp;<a title="Regulatory compliance" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regulatory_compliance">compliance</a>&nbsp;of a system or component with specified&nbsp;<a title="Functional requirement" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Functional_requirement">functional requirements</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;It occurs after&nbsp;<a title="Unit testing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unit_testing">unit testing</a>&nbsp;and before&nbsp;<a title="Software verification and validation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_verification_and_validation">validation testing</a>. Integration testing takes as its input&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Module (programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Module_(programming)">modules</a>&nbsp;that have been unit tested, groups them in larger aggregates, applies tests defined in an integration&nbsp;<a title="Test plan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Test_plan">test plan</a>&nbsp;to those aggregates, and delivers as its output the integrated system ready for&nbsp;<a title="System testing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/System_testing">system testing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Intellectual property" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intellectual_property">Intellectual property</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (IP), is a category of&nbsp;<a title="Property" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Property">property</a>&nbsp;that includes intangible creations of the human intellect.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;There are many types of intellectual property, and some countries recognize more than others.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;The most well-known types are&nbsp;<a title="Copyright" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copyright">copyrights</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Patent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patent">patents</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Trademark" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trademark">trademarks</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Trade secret" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trade_secret">trade secrets</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Intelligent agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligent_agent">Intelligent agent</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Interface (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interface_(computing)">Interface</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a shared boundary across which two or more separate components of a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computer system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_system">computer system</a>&nbsp;exchange information. The exchange can be between&nbsp;<a title="Software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software">software</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Computer hardware" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_hardware">computer hardware</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Peripheral" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peripheral">peripheral</a>&nbsp;devices,&nbsp;<a title="User interface" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/User_interface">humans</a>, and combinations of these.<sup id="cite_ref-HookwayInterface14_110-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;Some computer hardware devices, such as a&nbsp;<a title="Touchscreen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Touchscreen">touchscreen</a>, can both send and receive data through the interface, while others such as a mouse or microphone may only provide an interface to send data to a given system.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Internal documentation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internal_documentation">Internal documentation</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; Computer&nbsp;<a title="Software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software">software</a>&nbsp;is said to have Internal Documentation if the notes on how and why various parts of code operate is included within the&nbsp;<a title="Source code" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Source_code">source code</a>&nbsp;as comments. It is often combined with meaningful&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Variable (programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variable_(programming)">variable</a>&nbsp;names with the intention of providing potential future programmers a means of understanding the workings of the code. This contrasts with external&nbsp;<a title="Documentation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Documentation">documentation</a>, where programmers keep their notes and explanations in a separate document.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Internet" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet">Internet</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; The Internet (<a title="Portmanteau" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portmanteau">portmanteau</a>&nbsp;of interconnected network) is the global system of interconnected&nbsp;<a title="Computer network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_network">computer networks</a>&nbsp;that use the&nbsp;<a title="Internet protocol suite" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet_protocol_suite">Internet protocol suite</a>&nbsp;(TCP/IP) to link devices worldwide. It is a&nbsp;<em>network of networks</em>&nbsp;that consists of private, public, academic, business, and government networks of local to global scope, linked by a broad array of electronic, wireless, and optical networking technologies.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Internet bot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet_bot">Internet bot</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; also known as a&nbsp;<a title="World Wide Web" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Wide_Web">web</a>&nbsp;robot, robot or simply bot, is a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Software application" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_application">software application</a>&nbsp;that runs automated tasks (scripts) over the&nbsp;<a title="Internet" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet">Internet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;Typically, bots perform tasks that are both simple and structurally repetitive, at a much higher rate than would be possible for a human alone. The largest use of bots is in&nbsp;<a title="Web crawler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_crawler">web spidering</a>&nbsp;(<em>web crawler</em>), in which an automated script fetches, analyzes and files information from web servers at many times the speed of a&nbsp;<a title="Human" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human">human</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Interpreter (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interpreter_(computing)">Interpreter</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">computer program</a>&nbsp;that directly&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Execution (computers)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Execution_(computers)">executes</a>&nbsp;instructions written in a&nbsp;<a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language">programming</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Scripting language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scripting_language">scripting language</a>, without requiring them previously to have been&nbsp;<a title="Compiler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compiler">compiled</a>&nbsp;into a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Machine language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_language">machine language</a>&nbsp;program.</li>
<li><strong><a class="mw-redirect" title="Invariant (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Invariant_(computer_science)">Invariant</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Iteration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iteration">Iteration</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="J" class="mw-headline">J</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><strong><a title="Java (programming language)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Java_(programming_language)">Java</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="General-purpose language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General-purpose_language">general-purpose</a>&nbsp;<a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language">programming language</a>&nbsp;that is&nbsp;<a title="Class-based programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class-based_programming">class-based</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Object-oriented programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object-oriented_programming">object-oriented</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDECODER1_113-0" class="reference"></sup>(although not a&nbsp;<em>pure</em>&nbsp;OO language<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"></sup>), and designed to have as few implementation&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Dependency (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dependency_(computer_science)">dependencies</a>&nbsp;as possible. It is intended to let&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Application developer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_developer">application developers</a>&nbsp;"<a title="Write once, run anywhere" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Write_once,_run_anywhere">write once, run anywhere</a>" (WORA),<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;meaning that&nbsp;<a title="Compiler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compiler">compiled</a>&nbsp;Java code can run on all platforms that support Java without the need for recompilation.<sup id="cite_ref-design_goals_116-0" class="reference"></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="K" class="mw-headline">K</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><strong><a title="Kernel (operating system)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kernel_(operating_system)">Kernel</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; When referring to an&nbsp;<a title="Operating system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operating_system">operating system</a>, the kernel is the first section of the&nbsp;<a title="Operating system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operating_system">operating system</a>&nbsp;to load into&nbsp;<a title="Memory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Memory">memory</a>. As the center of the&nbsp;<a title="Operating system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operating_system">operating system</a>, the kernel needs to be small, efficient and loaded into a protected area in the memory so as not to be overwritten. It can be responsible for such things as disk drive management, file management, memory management, process management, etc.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="L" class="mw-headline">L</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><strong><a title="Library (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Library_(computing)">Library (computing)</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a collection of&nbsp;<a title="Non-volatile memory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-volatile_memory">non-volatile</a>&nbsp;resources used by&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">computer programs</a>, often for&nbsp;<a title="Software development" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_development">software development</a>. These may include configuration data, documentation, help data, message templates,&nbsp;<a title="Code reuse" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Code_reuse">pre-written code</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Subroutine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subroutine">subroutines</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Class (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_(computer_science)">classes</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Value (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Value_(computer_science)">values</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Data type" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_type">type</a>&nbsp;specifications.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Linear search" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linear_search">Linear search</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; or sequential search, is a method for finding an element within a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="List (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_(computing)">list</a>. It sequentially checks each element of the list until a match is found or the whole list has been searched.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKnuth1998&sect;6.1_(&quot;Sequential_search&quot;)_117-0" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Linked list" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linked_list">Linked list</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a linear collection of data elements, whose order is not given by their physical placement in memory. Instead, each element&nbsp;<a title="Pointer (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pointer_(computer_programming)">points</a>&nbsp;to the next. It is a&nbsp;<a title="Data structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_structure">data structure</a>&nbsp;consisting of a collection of&nbsp;<a title="Node (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Node_(computer_science)">nodes</a>&nbsp;which together represent a&nbsp;<a title="Sequence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sequence">sequence</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Linker (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linker_(computing)">Linker</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; or link editor, is a computer&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="System utility" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/System_utility">utility</a>&nbsp;program that takes one or more&nbsp;<a title="Object file" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object_file">object files</a>&nbsp;generated by a&nbsp;<a title="Compiler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compiler">compiler</a>&nbsp;or an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Assembler (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assembler_(computing)">assembler</a>&nbsp;and combines them into a single&nbsp;<a title="Executable" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executable">executable</a>&nbsp;file,&nbsp;<a title="Library (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Library_(computing)">library</a>&nbsp;file, or another 'object' file. A simpler version that writes its output directly to memory is called the&nbsp;<em>loader</em>, though&nbsp;<a title="Loader (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loader_(computing)">loading</a>&nbsp;is typically considered a separate process.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="List (abstract data type)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_(abstract_data_type)">List</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; or sequence, is an&nbsp;<a title="Abstract data type" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abstract_data_type">abstract data type</a>&nbsp;that represents a countable number of ordered&nbsp;<a title="Value (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Value_(computer_science)">values</a>, where the same value may occur more than once. An instance of a list is a computer representation of the&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematical</a>&nbsp;concept of a finite&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Sequence (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sequence_(mathematics)">sequence</a>; the (potentially) infinite analog of a list is a&nbsp;<a title="Stream (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stream_(computing)">stream</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"></sup><sup class="reference">:&sect;3.5</sup>&nbsp;Lists are a basic example of&nbsp;<a title="Container (abstract data type)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Container_(abstract_data_type)">containers</a>, as they contain other values. If the same value occurs multiple times, each occurrence is considered a distinct item.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Loader (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loader_(computing)">Loader</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is the part of an&nbsp;<a title="Operating system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operating_system">operating system</a>&nbsp;that is responsible for loading&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">programs</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Library (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Library_(computing)">libraries</a>. It is one of the essential stages in the process of starting a program, as it places programs into memory and prepares them for execution. Loading a program involves reading the contents of the&nbsp;<a title="Executable" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executable">executable file</a>&nbsp;containing the program instructions into memory, and then carrying out other required preparatory tasks to prepare the executable for running. Once loading is complete, the operating system starts the program by passing control to the loaded program code.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Logic error" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic_error">Logic error</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computer programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_programming">computer programming</a>, a logic error is a&nbsp;<a title="Software bug" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_bug">bug</a>&nbsp;in a program that causes it to operate incorrectly, but not to terminate abnormally (or&nbsp;<a title="Crash (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crash_(computing)">crash</a>). A logic error produces unintended or undesired output or other behaviour, although it may not immediately be recognized as such.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Logic programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic_programming">Logic programming</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a type of&nbsp;<a title="Programming paradigm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_paradigm">programming paradigm</a>&nbsp;which is largely based on&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Formal logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_logic">formal logic</a>. Any program written in a logic&nbsp;<a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language">programming language</a>&nbsp;is a set of sentences in logical form, expressing facts and rules about some problem domain. Major logic programming language families include&nbsp;<a title="Prolog" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prolog">Prolog</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Answer set programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Answer_set_programming">answer set programming</a>&nbsp;(ASP) and&nbsp;<a title="Datalog" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Datalog">Datalog</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="M" class="mw-headline">M</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><strong><a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">Machine learning</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (ML), is the&nbsp;<a title="Branches of science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Branches_of_science">scientific study</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithms</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Statistical model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_model">statistical models</a>&nbsp;that&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computer systems" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_systems">computer systems</a>&nbsp;use to perform a specific task without using explicit instructions, relying on patterns and&nbsp;<a title="Inference" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inference">inference</a>&nbsp;instead. It is seen as a subset of&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>. Machine learning algorithms build a&nbsp;<a title="Mathematical model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_model">mathematical model</a>&nbsp;based on sample data, known as "<a class="mw-redirect" title="Training data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Training_data">training data</a>", in order to make predictions or decisions without being explicitly programmed to perform the task.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Machine vision" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_vision">Machine vision</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (MV), is the technology and methods used to provide imaging-based automatic inspection and analysis for such applications as automatic inspection,&nbsp;<a title="Process control" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Process_control">process control</a>, and robot guidance, usually in industry. Machine vision refers to many technologies, software and hardware products, integrated systems, actions, methods and expertise. Machine vision as a&nbsp;<a title="Systems engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Systems_engineering">systems engineering</a>&nbsp;discipline can be considered distinct from&nbsp;<a title="Computer vision" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_vision">computer vision</a>, a form of&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>. It attempts to integrate existing technologies in new ways and apply them to solve real world problems. The term is the prevalent one for these functions in industrial automation environments but is also used for these functions in other environments such as security and vehicle guidance.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Mathematical logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_logic">Mathematical logic</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a subfield of&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>&nbsp;exploring the applications of formal&nbsp;<a title="Logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic">logic</a>&nbsp;to mathematics. It bears close connections to&nbsp;<a title="Metamathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metamathematics">metamathematics</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="Foundations of mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foundations_of_mathematics">foundations of mathematics</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Theoretical computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theoretical_computer_science">theoretical computer science</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;The unifying themes in mathematical logic include the study of the expressive power of&nbsp;<a title="Formal system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_system">formal systems</a>&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<a title="Deductive reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deductive_reasoning">deductive</a>&nbsp;power of formal&nbsp;<a title="Mathematical proof" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_proof">proof</a>&nbsp;systems.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Matrix (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matrix_(mathematics)">Matrix</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>, a matrix, (plural matrices), is a&nbsp;<a title="Rectangle" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rectangle">rectangular</a>&nbsp;<em><a class="extiw" title="wikt:array" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/array">array</a></em><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;(see&nbsp;<a title="Irregular matrix" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irregular_matrix">irregular matrix</a>) of&nbsp;<a title="Number" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Number">numbers</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Symbol (formal)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symbol_(formal)">symbols</a>, or&nbsp;<a title="Expression (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expression_(mathematics)">expressions</a>, arranged in&nbsp;<em><a class="extiw" title="wikt:row" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/row">rows</a></em>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<em><a class="extiw" title="wikt:column" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/column">columns</a></em>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Computer data storage" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_data_storage">Memory</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; Computer data storage, often called storage, is a technology consisting of&nbsp;<a title="Computer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer">computer</a>&nbsp;components and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Data storage device" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_storage_device">recording media</a>&nbsp;that are used to retain digital&nbsp;<a title="Data (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_(computing)">data</a>. It is a core function and fundamental component of computers.<sup id="cite_ref-Patterson_126-0" class="reference"></sup><sup class="reference">:15&ndash;16</sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Merge sort" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Merge_sort">Merge sort</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (also commonly spelled mergesort), is an efficient, general-purpose,&nbsp;<a title="Comparison sort" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comparison_sort">comparison-based</a>&nbsp;<a title="Sorting algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sorting_algorithm">sorting algorithm</a>. Most implementations produce a&nbsp;<a title="Sorting algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sorting_algorithm#Stability">stable sort</a>, which means that the order of equal elements is the same in the input and output. Merge sort is a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Divide and conquer algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Divide_and_conquer_algorithm">divide and conquer algorithm</a>&nbsp;that was invented by&nbsp;<a title="John von Neumann" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann">John von Neumann</a>&nbsp;in 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;A detailed description and analysis of bottom-up mergesort appeared in a report by&nbsp;<a title="Herman Goldstine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herman_Goldstine">Goldstine</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="John von Neumann" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann">von Neumann</a>&nbsp;as early as 1948.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Method (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Method_(computer_programming)">Method</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; in&nbsp;<a title="Object-oriented programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object-oriented_programming">object-oriented programming</a>&nbsp;(OOP), is a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Procedure (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Procedure_(computer_science)">procedure</a>&nbsp;associated with a&nbsp;<a title="Message passing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Message_passing">message</a>&nbsp;and an&nbsp;<a title="Object (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object_(computer_science)">object</a>. An object consists of data and behavior. The data and behavior comprise an interface, which specifies how the object may be utilized by any of various consumers<sup id="cite_ref-consumerdef001a_129-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;of the object.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Software development process" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_development_process">Methodology</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Software engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_engineering">software engineering</a>, a software development process is the process of dividing&nbsp;<a title="Software development" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_development">software development</a>&nbsp;work into distinct phases to improve&nbsp;<a title="Software design" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_design">design</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Software product management" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_product_management">product management</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Software project management" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_project_management">project management</a>. It is also known as a software development life cycle (SDLC). The methodology may include the pre-definition of specific&nbsp;<a title="Deliverable" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deliverable">deliverables</a>&nbsp;and artifacts that are created and completed by a project team to develop or maintain an application.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Modem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modem">Modem</a></strong>- (a&nbsp;<a title="Portmanteau" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portmanteau">portmanteau</a>&nbsp;of modulator-demodulator) is a&nbsp;<a title="Computer hardware" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_hardware">hardware</a>&nbsp;device that converts data into a format suitable for a&nbsp;<a title="Transmission medium" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transmission_medium">transmission medium</a>&nbsp;so that it can be transmitted from one computer to another (historically along telephone wires). A modem&nbsp;<a title="Modulation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modulation#Digital_modulation_methods">modulates</a>&nbsp;one or more&nbsp;<a title="Carrier wave" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carrier_wave">carrier wave</a>&nbsp;signals to encode&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Digital information" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_information">digital information</a>&nbsp;for transmission and&nbsp;<a title="Demodulation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demodulation">demodulates</a>&nbsp;signals to decode the transmitted information. The goal is to produce a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Signal (electronics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Signal_(electronics)">signal</a>&nbsp;that can be transmitted easily and decoded reliably to reproduce the original digital data. Modems can be used with almost any means of transmitting analog signals from&nbsp;<a title="Light-emitting diode" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Light-emitting_diode">light-emitting diodes</a>&nbsp;to&nbsp;<a title="Radio" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radio">radio</a>. A common type of modem is one that turns the&nbsp;<a title="Digital data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_data">digital data</a>&nbsp;of a&nbsp;<a title="Computer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer">computer</a>&nbsp;into modulated&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Electrical signal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrical_signal">electrical signal</a>&nbsp;for transmission over&nbsp;<a title="Telephone line" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telephone_line">telephone lines</a>&nbsp;and demodulated by another modem at the receiver side to recover the digital data.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="N" class="mw-headline">N</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><strong><a title="Natural language processing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language_processing">Natural language processing</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (NLP), is a subfield of&nbsp;<a title="Linguistics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linguistics">linguistics</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Information engineering (field)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_engineering_(field)">information engineering</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;concerned with the interactions between computers and human (natural) languages, in particular how to program computers to process and analyze large amounts of&nbsp;<a title="Natural language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language">natural language</a>&nbsp;data. Challenges in natural language processing frequently involve&nbsp;<a title="Speech recognition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speech_recognition">speech recognition</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Natural language understanding" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language_understanding">natural language understanding</a>, and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Natural language generation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language_generation">natural language generation</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Number theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Number_theory">Number theory</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a branch of&nbsp;<a title="Pure mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pure_mathematics">pure mathematics</a>&nbsp;devoted primarily to the study of the&nbsp;<a title="Integer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Integer">integers</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Arithmetic function" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arithmetic_function">integer-valued functions</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Numerical analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numerical_analysis">Numerical analysis</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is the study of&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithms</a>&nbsp;that use numerical&nbsp;<a title="Approximation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Approximation">approximation</a>&nbsp;(as opposed to&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Symbolic computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symbolic_computation">symbolic manipulations</a>) for the problems of&nbsp;<a title="Mathematical analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_analysis">mathematical analysis</a>&nbsp;(as distinguished from&nbsp;<a title="Discrete mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discrete_mathematics">discrete mathematics</a>).</li>
<li><strong><a title="Numerical method" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numerical_method">Numerical method</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Numerical analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numerical_analysis">numerical analysis</a>, a numerical method is a mathematical tool designed to solve numerical problems. The implementation of a numerical method with an appropriate convergence check in a programming language is called a numerical algorithm.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="O" class="mw-headline">O</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><strong><a title="Object (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object_(computer_science)">Object</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; An object can be a&nbsp;<a title="Variable (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variable_(computer_science)">variable</a>, a&nbsp;<a title="Data structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_structure">data structure</a>, a&nbsp;<a title="Subroutine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subroutine">function</a>, or a&nbsp;<a title="Method (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Method_(computer_programming)">method</a>, and as such, is a&nbsp;<a title="Value (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Value_(computer_science)">value</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Memory address" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Memory_address">memory</a>&nbsp;referenced by an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Identifier (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Identifier_(computer_programming)">identifier</a>. In the&nbsp;<a title="Class-based programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class-based_programming">class-based</a>&nbsp;<a title="Object-oriented programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object-oriented_programming">object-oriented programming</a>&nbsp;paradigm,&nbsp;<em>object</em>&nbsp;refers to a particular&nbsp;<a title="Instance (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instance_(computer_science)">instance</a>&nbsp;of a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Class (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_(computer_science)">class</a>, where the object can be a combination of variables, functions, and data structures. In&nbsp;<a title="Relational model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Relational_model">relational</a>&nbsp;<a title="Database" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Database">database</a>&nbsp;management, an object can be a table or column, or an association between data and a database entity (such as relating a person's age to a specific person).<sup id="cite_ref-Oppel_131-0" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Object code" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object_code">Object code</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; or object module, is the product of a&nbsp;<a title="Compiler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compiler">compiler</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;In a general sense object code is a sequence of&nbsp;<a title="Statement (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statement_(computer_science)">statements</a>&nbsp;or instructions in a computer language,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;usually a&nbsp;<a title="Machine code" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_code">machine code</a>&nbsp;language (i.e.,&nbsp;<a title="Binary file" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Binary_file">binary</a>) or an intermediate language such as&nbsp;<a title="Register transfer language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Register_transfer_language">register transfer language</a>&nbsp;(RTL). The term indicates that the code is the&nbsp;<a title="Goal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Goal">goal</a>&nbsp;or result of the compiling process, with some early sources referring to source code as a "subject program."</li>
<li><strong><a title="Object-oriented analysis and design" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object-oriented_analysis_and_design">Object-oriented analysis and design</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (OOAD), is a technical approach for analyzing and designing an application, system, or business by applying&nbsp;<a title="Object-oriented programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object-oriented_programming">object-oriented programming</a>, as well as using visual modeling throughout the software development process to guide stakeholder communication and product quality.</li>
<li><strong><a class="mw-redirect" title="Object oriented programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object_oriented_programming">Object oriented programming</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (OOP), is a&nbsp;<a title="Programming paradigm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_paradigm">programming paradigm</a>&nbsp;based on the concept of "<a title="Object (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object_(computer_science)">objects</a>", which can contain&nbsp;<a title="Data" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data">data</a>, in the form of&nbsp;<a title="Field (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Field_(computer_science)">fields</a>&nbsp;(often known as&nbsp;<em>attributes</em>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<em>properties</em>), and code, in the form of procedures (often known as&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Method (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Method_(computer_science)">methods</a></em>). A feature of objects is an object's procedures that can access and often modify the data fields of the object with which they are associated (objects have a notion of "<a title="This (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/This_(computer_programming)">this</a>" or "self"). In OOP, computer programs are designed by making them out of objects that interact with one another.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;OOP languages are diverse, but the most popular ones are&nbsp;<a title="Class-based programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class-based_programming">class-based</a>, meaning that objects are&nbsp;<a title="Instance (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instance_(computer_science)">instances</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Class (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_(computer_science)">classes</a>, which also determine their&nbsp;<a title="Data type" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_type">types</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Open-source software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open-source_software">Open-source software</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (OSS), is a type of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computer software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_software">computer software</a>&nbsp;in which&nbsp;<a title="Source code" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Source_code">source code</a>&nbsp;is released under a&nbsp;<a title="Open-source license" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open-source_license">license</a>&nbsp;in which the&nbsp;<a title="Copyright" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copyright">copyright</a>&nbsp;holder grants users the rights to study, change, and&nbsp;<a title="Software distribution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_distribution">distribute the software</a>&nbsp;to anyone and for any purpose.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;Open-source&nbsp;<a title="Software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software">software</a>&nbsp;may be developed in a&nbsp;<a title="Open-source model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open-source_model">collaborative public manner</a>. Open-source software is a prominent example of&nbsp;<a title="Open collaboration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open_collaboration">open collaboration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Open_Collaboration_137-0" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Operating system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operating_system">Operating system</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (OS), is&nbsp;<a title="System software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/System_software">system software</a>&nbsp;that manages&nbsp;<a title="Computer hardware" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_hardware">computer hardware</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computer software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_software">software</a>&nbsp;resources, and provides common&nbsp;<a title="Daemon (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daemon_(computing)">services</a>&nbsp;for&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">computer programs</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Optical fiber" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optical_fiber">Optical fiber</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a flexible,&nbsp;<a title="Transparency and translucency" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transparency_and_translucency">transparent</a>&nbsp;<a title="Fiber" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fiber">fiber</a>&nbsp;made by&nbsp;<a title="Drawing (manufacturing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drawing_(manufacturing)">drawing</a>&nbsp;<a title="Glass" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glass">glass</a>&nbsp;(<a class="mw-redirect" title="Silica" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silica">silica</a>) or plastic to a diameter slightly thicker than that of a&nbsp;<a title="Hair's breadth" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hair%27s_breadth">human hair</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;Optical fibers are used most often as a means to transmit light between the two ends of the fiber and find wide usage in&nbsp;<a title="Fiber-optic communication" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fiber-optic_communication">fiber-optic communications</a>, where they permit transmission over longer distances and at higher&nbsp;<a title="Bandwidth (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bandwidth_(computing)">bandwidths</a>&nbsp;(data rates) than electrical cables. Fibers are used instead of&nbsp;<a title="Metal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metal">metal</a>&nbsp;wires because signals travel along them with less&nbsp;<a title="Attenuation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attenuation">loss</a>; in addition, fibers are immune to&nbsp;<a title="Electromagnetic interference" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electromagnetic_interference">electromagnetic interference</a>, a problem from which metal wires suffer.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="P" class="mw-headline">P</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><strong><a title="Pair programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pair_programming">Pair programming</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is an&nbsp;<a title="Agile software development" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agile_software_development">agile software development</a>&nbsp;technique in which two&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computer programmer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_programmer">programmers</a>&nbsp;work together at one workstation. One, the&nbsp;<em>driver</em>, writes&nbsp;<a title="Source code" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Source_code">code</a>&nbsp;while the other, the&nbsp;<em>observer</em>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<em>navigator</em>,<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;<a title="Code review" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Code_review">reviews</a>&nbsp;each line of code as it is typed in. The two programmers switch roles frequently.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Parallel computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parallel_computing">Parallel computing</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a type of&nbsp;<a title="Computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computing">computation</a>&nbsp;in which many calculations or the execution of&nbsp;<a title="Process (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Process_(computing)">processes</a>&nbsp;are carried out simultaneously.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;Large problems can often be divided into smaller ones, which can then be solved at the same time. There are several different forms of parallel computing:&nbsp;<a title="Bit-level parallelism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bit-level_parallelism">bit-level</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Instruction-level parallelism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instruction-level_parallelism">instruction-level</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Data parallelism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_parallelism">data</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Task parallelism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Task_parallelism">task parallelism</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Parameter (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parameter_(computer_programming)">Parameter</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computer programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_programming">computer programming</a>, a parameter or a&nbsp;<em>formal argument</em>, is a special kind of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Variable (programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variable_(programming)">variable</a>, used in a&nbsp;<a title="Subroutine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subroutine">subroutine</a>&nbsp;to refer to one of the pieces of data provided as input to the subroutine.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_computer_science#cite_note-142">[b]</a></sup>&nbsp;These pieces of data are the values<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;of the arguments (often called&nbsp;<em>actual arguments</em>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<em>actual parameters</em>) with which the subroutine is going to be called/invoked. An ordered list of parameters is usually included in the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Function signature" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Function_signature">definition of a subroutine</a>, so that, each time the subroutine is called, its arguments for that call are evaluated, and the resulting values can be assigned to the corresponding parameters.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Peripheral" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peripheral">Peripheral</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Postcondition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Postcondition">Postcondition</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computer programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_programming">computer programming</a>, a postcondition is a condition or&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Predicate (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Predicate_(mathematics)">predicate</a>&nbsp;that must always be true just after the execution of some section of code or after an operation in a&nbsp;<a title="Formal specification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_specification">formal specification</a>. Postconditions are sometimes tested using&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Assertion (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assertion_(computing)">assertions</a>&nbsp;within the code itself. Often, postconditions are simply included in the documentation of the affected section of code.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Precondition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Precondition">Precondition</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computer programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_programming">computer programming</a>, a precondition is a condition or&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Predicate (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Predicate_(mathematics)">predicate</a>&nbsp;that must always be true just prior to the execution of some section of&nbsp;<a title="Code" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Code">code</a>&nbsp;or before an operation in a&nbsp;<a title="Formal specification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_specification">formal specification</a>. If a precondition is violated, the effect of the section of&nbsp;<a title="Code" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Code">code</a>&nbsp;becomes undefined and thus may or may not carry out its intended work.&nbsp;<a title="Computer security" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_security">Security</a>&nbsp;problems can arise due to incorrect preconditions.</li>
<li><strong><a class="mw-redirect" title="Primary storage" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Primary_storage">Primary storage</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Primitive data type" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Primitive_data_type">Primitive data type</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Priority queue" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Priority_queue">Priority queue</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is an&nbsp;<a title="Abstract data type" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abstract_data_type">abstract data type</a>&nbsp;which is like a regular&nbsp;<a title="Queue (abstract data type)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Queue_(abstract_data_type)">queue</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Stack (abstract data type)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stack_(abstract_data_type)">stack</a>&nbsp;data structure, but where additionally each element has a "priority" associated with it. In a priority queue, an element with high priority is served before an element with low priority. In some implementations, if two elements have the same priority, they are served according to the order in which they were enqueued, while in other implementations, ordering of elements with the same priority is undefined.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Procedural programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Procedural_programming">Procedural programming</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Program lifecycle phase" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Program_lifecycle_phase">Program lifecycle phase</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; Program lifecycle phases are the stages a&nbsp;<a title="Computer program" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program">computer program</a>&nbsp;undergoes, from initial creation to deployment and&nbsp;<a title="Execution (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Execution_(computing)">execution</a>. The phases are edit time, compile time, link time, distribution time, installation time, load time, and run time.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language">Programming language</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Formal language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_language">formal language</a>, which comprises a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Instruction set" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instruction_set">set of instructions</a>&nbsp;that produce various kinds of&nbsp;<a title="Input/output" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Input/output">output</a>. Programming languages are used in&nbsp;<a title="Computer programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_programming">computer programming</a>&nbsp;to implement&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithms</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Programming language implementation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language_implementation">Programming language implementation</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Programming language theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language_theory">Programming language theory</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Prolog" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prolog">Prolog</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Python (programming language)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Python_(programming_language)">Python</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="Q" class="mw-headline">Q</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><strong><a title="Quantum computing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_computing">Quantum computing</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is the use of&nbsp;<a title="Quantum mechanics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_mechanics">quantum-mechanical</a>&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Phenomena" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phenomena">phenomena</a>&nbsp;such as&nbsp;<a title="Quantum superposition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_superposition">superposition</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Quantum entanglement" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_entanglement">entanglement</a>&nbsp;to perform&nbsp;<a title="Computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computation">computation</a>. A quantum computer is used to perform such computation, which can be implemented theoretically or physically.<sup id="cite_ref-2018Report_146-0" class="reference"></sup><sup class="reference">:I-5</sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Queue (abstract data type)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Queue_(abstract_data_type)">Queue</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a title="Collection (abstract data type)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collection_(abstract_data_type)">collection</a>&nbsp;in which the entities in the collection are kept in order and the principal (or only) operations on the collection are the addition of entities to the rear terminal position, known as&nbsp;<em>enqueue</em>, and removal of entities from the front terminal position, known as&nbsp;<em>dequeue</em>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Quicksort" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quicksort">Quicksort</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (sometimes called&nbsp;<em>partition-exchange sort) is an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Algorithm efficiency" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm_efficiency">efficient</a>&nbsp;<a title="Sorting algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sorting_algorithm">sorting algorithm</a>, serving as a systematic method for placing the elements of a&nbsp;<a title="Random access" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Random_access">random access</a>&nbsp;<a title="Computer file" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_file">file</a>&nbsp;or an&nbsp;<a title="Array data structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Array_data_structure">array</a>&nbsp;in order.</em></li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="R" class="mw-headline">R</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><strong><a title="R (programming language)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/R_(programming_language)">R programming language</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Radix" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radix">Radix</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Numeral system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numeral_system">digital numeral systems</a>, the radix, or&nbsp;<strong>base</strong>, is the number of unique&nbsp;<a title="Numerical digit" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numerical_digit">digits</a>, including the digit zero, used to represent numbers in a&nbsp;<a title="Positional notation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Positional_notation">positional</a>&nbsp;<a title="Numeral system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numeral_system">numeral system</a>. For example, for the decimal/denary system (the most common system in use today) the radix (base number) is ten, because it uses the ten digits from 0 through 9.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Recursion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recursion">Recursion</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; occurs when a thing is defined in terms of itself or of its type. Recursion is used in a variety of disciplines ranging from&nbsp;<a title="Linguistics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linguistics">linguistics</a>&nbsp;to&nbsp;<a title="Logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic">logic</a>. The most common application of recursion is in&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>, where a&nbsp;<a title="Function (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Function_(mathematics)">function</a>&nbsp;being defined is applied within its own definition. While this apparently defines an infinite number of instances (function values), it is often done in such a way that no infinite loop or infinite chain of references can occur.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Reference counting" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reference_counting">Reference counting</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a programming technique of storing the number of&nbsp;<a title="Reference (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reference_(computer_science)">references</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Pointer (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pointer_(computer_programming)">pointers</a>, or&nbsp;<a title="Handle (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Handle_(computing)">handles</a>&nbsp;to a resource, such as an object, a block of memory, disk space, and others. In&nbsp;<a title="Garbage collection (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Garbage_collection_(computer_science)">garbage collection</a>&nbsp;algorithms, reference counts may be used to deallocate objects which are no longer needed.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Relational database" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Relational_database">Relational database</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Reliability engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reliability_engineering">Reliability engineering</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a sub-discipline of&nbsp;<a title="Systems engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Systems_engineering">systems engineering</a>&nbsp;that emphasizes&nbsp;<a title="Dependability" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dependability">dependability</a>&nbsp;in the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Product lifecycle management" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Product_lifecycle_management">lifecycle management</a>&nbsp;of a&nbsp;<a title="Product (business)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Product_(business)">product</a>. Reliability describes the ability of a system or component to function under stated conditions for a specified period of time.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;Reliability is closely related to&nbsp;<a title="Availability" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Availability">availability</a>, which is typically described as the ability of a component or system to function at a specified moment or interval of time.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Regression testing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regression_testing">Regression testing</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (rarely&nbsp;<em>non-regression testing</em><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"></sup>) is re-running&nbsp;<a title="Functional testing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Functional_testing">functional</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Non-functional testing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-functional_testing">non-functional tests</a>&nbsp;to ensure that previously developed and tested software still performs after a change.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;If not, that would be called a&nbsp;<em><a title="Software regression" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_regression">regression</a></em>. Changes that may require regression testing include&nbsp;<a title="Software bug" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_bug">bug</a>&nbsp;fixes, software enhancements,&nbsp;<a title="Configuration file" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Configuration_file">configuration</a>&nbsp;changes, and even substitution of&nbsp;<a title="Electronic component" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electronic_component">electronic components</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;As regression test suites tend to grow with each found defect, test automation is frequently involved. Sometimes a&nbsp;<a title="Change impact analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Change_impact_analysis">change impact analysis</a>&nbsp;is performed to determine an appropriate subset of tests (<em>non-regression analysis</em><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"></sup>).</li>
<li><strong><a title="Requirements analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Requirements_analysis">Requirements analysis</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Systems engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Systems_engineering">systems engineering</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Software engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_engineering">software engineering</a>, requirements analysis focuses on the tasks that determine the needs or conditions to meet the new or altered product or project, taking account of the possibly conflicting&nbsp;<a title="Requirement" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Requirement">requirements</a>&nbsp;of the various&nbsp;<a title="Stakeholder (corporate)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stakeholder_(corporate)">stakeholders</a>,&nbsp;<em>analyzing, documenting, validating and managing</em>&nbsp;software or system requirements.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Robotics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robotics">Robotics</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is an&nbsp;<a title="Interdisciplinarity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interdisciplinarity">interdisciplinary</a>&nbsp;branch of&nbsp;<a title="List of engineering branches" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_engineering_branches">engineering</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Branch of science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Branch_of_science">science</a>&nbsp;that includes&nbsp;<a title="Mechanical engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mechanical_engineering">mechanical engineering</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Electronic engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electronic_engineering">electronic engineering</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Information engineering (field)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_engineering_(field)">information engineering</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Computer science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>, and others. Robotics involves design, construction, operation, and use of&nbsp;<a title="Robot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robot">robots</a>, as well as&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computer system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_system">computer systems</a>&nbsp;for their perception, control,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Sensory feedback" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sensory_feedback">sensory feedback</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Information processing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_processing">information processing</a>. The goal of robotics is to design intelligent machines that can help and assist humans in their day-to-day lives and keep everyone safe.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Round-off error" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Round-off_error">Round-off error</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; A roundoff error,<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;also called&nbsp;<strong>rounding error</strong>,<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;is the difference between the result produced by a given&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithm</a>&nbsp;using exact arithmetic and the result produced by the same algorithm using finite-precision, rounded arithmetic.<sup id="cite_ref-Forrester_2018_155-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;Rounding errors are due to inexactness in the representation of real numbers and the arithmetic operations done with them. This is a form of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Quantization error" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantization_error">quantization error</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;When using approximation&nbsp;<a title="Equation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equation">equations</a>&nbsp;or algorithms, especially when using finitely many digits to represent real numbers (which in theory have infinitely many digits), one of the goals of&nbsp;<a title="Numerical analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numerical_analysis">numerical analysis</a>&nbsp;is to&nbsp;<a title="Error analysis (mathematics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Error_analysis_(mathematics)">estimate</a>&nbsp;computation errors.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;Computation errors, also called&nbsp;<a title="Numerical error" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numerical_error">numerical errors</a>, include both&nbsp;<a title="Truncation error" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Truncation_error">truncation errors</a>&nbsp;and roundoff errors.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Router (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Router_(computing)">Router</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Networking device" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Networking_device">networking device</a>&nbsp;that forwards&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Data packet" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_packet">data packets</a>&nbsp;between&nbsp;<a title="Computer network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_network">computer networks</a>. Routers perform the traffic directing functions on the&nbsp;<a title="Internet" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet">Internet</a>. Data sent through the internet, such as a&nbsp;<a title="Web page" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_page">web page</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Email" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Email">email</a>, is in the form of data packets. A packet is typically&nbsp;<a title="Packet forwarding" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Packet_forwarding">forwarded</a>&nbsp;from one router to another router through the networks that constitute an&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Internetwork" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internetwork">internetwork</a>&nbsp;(e.g. the Internet) until it reaches its destination&nbsp;<a title="Node (networking)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Node_(networking)">node</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Routing table" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Routing_table">Routing table</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a class="mw-redirect" title="Run time (program lifecycle phase)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Run_time_(program_lifecycle_phase)">Run time</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a class="mw-redirect" title="Run time (program lifecycle phase)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Run_time_(program_lifecycle_phase)">Run time error</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="S" class="mw-headline">S</span></h2>
