<li><strong><a title="Search algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Search_algorithm">Search algorithm</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is any&nbsp;<a title="Algorithm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithm</a>&nbsp;which solves the&nbsp;<a title="Search problem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Search_problem">search problem</a>, namely, to retrieve information stored within some data structure, or calculated in the&nbsp;<a title="Feasible region" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feasible_region">search space</a>&nbsp;of a&nbsp;<a class="new" title="Problem domain (page does not exist)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Problem_domain&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1">problem domain</a>, either with&nbsp;<a title="Continuous or discrete variable" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continuous_or_discrete_variable">discrete or continuous values</a>.</li>

<h2><span id="T" class="mw-headline">T</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><strong><a title="Technical documentation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technical_documentation">Technical documentation</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In engineering,&nbsp;<strong>technical documentation</strong>&nbsp;refers to any type of&nbsp;<a title="Documentation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Documentation">documentation</a>&nbsp;that describes handling, functionality and architecture of a technical product or a product under&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Product development" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Product_development">development</a>&nbsp;or use.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;The intended recipient for product technical documentation is both the (proficient)&nbsp;<a title="End user" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/End_user">end user</a>&nbsp;as well as the administrator / service or&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Maintenance, repair and operations" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maintenance,_repair_and_operations">maintenance</a>&nbsp;technician. In contrast to a mere "cookbook"&nbsp;<a title="User guide" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/User_guide">manual</a>, technical documentation aims at providing enough information for a user to understand inner and outer dependencies of the product at hand.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Third-generation programming language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Third-generation_programming_language">Third-generation programming language</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Top-down and bottom-up design" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Top-down_and_bottom-up_design">Top-down and bottom-up design</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash;</li>
<li><strong><a title="Tree (data structure)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tree_(data_structure)">Tree</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a widely used&nbsp;<a title="Abstract data type" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abstract_data_type">abstract data type</a>&nbsp;(ADT) that simulates a hierarchical&nbsp;<a title="Tree structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tree_structure">tree structure</a>, with a root value and subtrees of children with a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_computer_science#Terminology">parent node</a>, represented as a set of linked&nbsp;<a title="Node (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Node_(computer_science)">nodes</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Type theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Type_theory">Type theory</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Logic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic">logic</a>, and computer science, a type theory is any of a class of&nbsp;<a title="Formal system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_system">formal systems</a>, some of which can serve as alternatives to&nbsp;<a title="Set theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Set_theory">set theory</a>&nbsp;as a&nbsp;<a title="Foundations of mathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foundations_of_mathematics">foundation for all mathematics</a>. In type theory, every "term" has a "type" and operations are restricted to terms of a certain type.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="U" class="mw-headline">U</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><strong><a title="Upload" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Upload">Upload</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computer network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_network">computer networks</a>, to&nbsp;<strong>upload</strong>&nbsp;is to send&nbsp;<a title="Data (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_(computing)">data</a>&nbsp;to a remote system such as a&nbsp;<a title="Server (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Server_(computing)">server</a>&nbsp;or another client so that the remote system can store a copy.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="URL" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/URL">Uniform Resource Locator</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (URL), colloquially termed a&nbsp;<strong>web address</strong>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEW3C2009_163-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;is a reference to a&nbsp;<a title="Web resource" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_resource">web resource</a>&nbsp;that specifies its location on a&nbsp;<a title="Computer network" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_network">computer network</a>&nbsp;and a mechanism for retrieving it. A URL is a specific type of&nbsp;<a title="Uniform Resource Identifier" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uniform_Resource_Identifier">Uniform Resource Identifier</a>&nbsp;(URI),<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERFC_39862005_165-0" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;although many people use the two terms interchangeably.&nbsp;URLs occur most commonly to reference web pages (<a class="mw-redirect" title="Http" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Http">http</a>), but are also used for file transfer (<a title="File Transfer Protocol" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File_Transfer_Protocol">ftp</a>), email (<a title="Mailto" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mailto">mailto</a>), database access (<a title="Java Database Connectivity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Java_Database_Connectivity">JDBC</a>), and many other applications.</li>
<li><strong><a title="URL" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/URL">URL</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; Uniform Resource Locator.</li>
<li><strong><a title="User agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/User_agent">User agent</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is software (a&nbsp;<a title="Software agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_agent">software agent</a>) that is acting on behalf of a&nbsp;<a title="User (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/User_(computing)">user</a>, such as a&nbsp;<a title="Web browser" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_browser">web browser</a>&nbsp;that "retrieves, renders and facilitates end user interaction with Web content".<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;An email reader is a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Mail user agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mail_user_agent">mail user agent</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="User interface" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/User_interface">User interface</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (UI), in the&nbsp;<a title="Industrial design" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrial_design">industrial design</a>&nbsp;field of&nbsp;<a title="Human&ndash;computer interaction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human%E2%80%93computer_interaction">human-computer interaction</a>, is the space where interactions between humans and machines occur. The goal of this interaction is to allow effective operation and control of the machine from the human end, whilst the machine simultaneously feeds back information that aids the operators'&nbsp;<a title="Decision-making" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decision-making">decision-making</a>&nbsp;process. Examples of this broad concept of user interfaces include the interactive aspects of computer&nbsp;<a title="Operating system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operating_system">operating systems</a>, hand&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Tools" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tools">tools</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Heavy machinery" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heavy_machinery">heavy machinery</a>&nbsp;operator controls, and&nbsp;<a title="Unit operation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unit_operation">process</a>&nbsp;controls. The design considerations applicable when creating user interfaces are related to or involve such disciplines as&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Ergonomics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ergonomics">ergonomics</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Psychology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Psychology">psychology</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="User interface design" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/User_interface_design">User interface design</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; or user interface engineering, is the&nbsp;<a title="Design" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Design">design</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="User interface" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/User_interface">user interfaces</a>&nbsp;for&nbsp;<a title="Machine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine">machines</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Software" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software">software</a>, such as&nbsp;<a title="Computer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer">computers</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Home appliance" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Home_appliance">home appliances</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Mobile device" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mobile_device">mobile devices</a>, and other&nbsp;<a title="Electronics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electronics">electronic devices</a>, with the focus on maximizing&nbsp;<a title="Usability" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Usability">usability</a>&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<a title="User experience" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/User_experience">user experience</a>. The goal of user interface design is to make the user's interaction as simple and efficient as possible, in terms of accomplishing user goals (<a title="User-centered design" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/User-centered_design">user-centered design</a>).</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="V" class="mw-headline">V</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><strong><a title="Variable (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variable_(computer_science)">Variable</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Computer programming" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_programming">computer programming</a>, a variable, or scalar, is a storage location (identified by a&nbsp;<a title="Memory address" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Memory_address">memory address</a>) paired with an associated&nbsp;<a title="Symbol" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symbol">symbolic name</a>&nbsp;(an&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Identifier (computer programming)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Identifier_(computer_programming)">identifier</a></em>), which contains some known or unknown quantity of information referred to as a&nbsp;<em><a title="Value (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Value_(computer_science)">value</a></em>. The variable name is the usual way to&nbsp;<a title="Reference (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reference_(computer_science)">reference</a>&nbsp;the stored value, in addition to referring to the variable itself, depending on the context. This separation of name and content allows the name to be used independently of the exact information it represents. The identifier in computer&nbsp;<a title="Source code" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Source_code">source code</a>&nbsp;can be&nbsp;<a title="Name binding" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Name_binding">bound</a>&nbsp;to a&nbsp;<a title="Value (computer science)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Value_(computer_science)">value</a>&nbsp;during&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Run time (program lifecycle phase)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Run_time_(program_lifecycle_phase)">run time</a>, and the value of the variable may thus change during the course of&nbsp;<a title="Execution (computing)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Execution_(computing)">program execution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"></sup></li>
<li><strong><a title="Virtual machine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virtual_machine">Virtual machine</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (VM), is an&nbsp;<a title="Emulator" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emulator">emulation</a>&nbsp;of a computer system. Virtual machines are based on&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Computer architectures" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_architectures">computer architectures</a>&nbsp;and provide functionality of a physical computer. Their implementations may involve specialized hardware, software, or a combination.</li>
<li><strong><a title="V-Model (software development)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/V-Model_(software_development)">V-Model</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; In&nbsp;<a title="Software development" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_development">software development</a>, the V-model<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"></sup>&nbsp;represents a&nbsp;<a title="Software development process" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_development_process">development process</a>&nbsp;that may be considered an extension of the&nbsp;<a title="Waterfall model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Waterfall_model">waterfall model</a>, and is an example of the more&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="V-model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/V-model">general V-model</a>. Instead of moving down in a linear way, the process steps are bent upwards after the&nbsp;<a title="Source code" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Source_code">coding</a>&nbsp;phase, to form the typical V shape. The V-Model demonstrates the relationships between each phase of the development life cycle and its associated phase of&nbsp;<a title="Software testing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_testing">testing</a>. The horizontal and vertical axes represent time or project completeness (left-to-right) and level of abstraction (coarsest-grain abstraction uppermost), respectively.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="W" class="mw-headline">W</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><strong><a title="WAV" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WAV">WAV</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; Waveform Audio File Format.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Waterfall model" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Waterfall_model">Waterfall model</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a breakdown of project activities into linear&nbsp;<a title="Sequence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sequence">sequential</a>&nbsp;phases, where each phase depends on the deliverables of the previous one and corresponds to a specialisation of tasks. The approach is typical for certain areas of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Engineering design" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Engineering_design">engineering design</a>. In&nbsp;<a title="Software development process" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_development_process">software development</a>, it tends to be among the less iterative and flexible approaches, as progress flows in largely one direction ("downwards" like a&nbsp;<a title="Waterfall" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Waterfall">waterfall</a>) through the phases of conception, initiation,&nbsp;<a title="Analysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Analysis">analysis</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Software design" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_design">design</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Software construction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_construction">construction</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Software testing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_testing">testing</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Implementation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Implementation">deployment</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Software maintenance" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_maintenance">maintenance</a>.</li>
<li><strong><a title="WAV" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WAV">Waveform Audio File Format</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; (WAVE, or WAV due to its&nbsp;<a title="Filename extension" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Filename_extension">filename extension</a>), is an&nbsp;<a title="Audio file format" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Audio_file_format">audio file format</a>&nbsp;standard, developed by&nbsp;<a title="Microsoft" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsoft">Microsoft</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="International Business Machines" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Business_Machines">IBM</a>, for storing an audio bitstream on&nbsp;<a title="Personal computer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Personal_computer">PCs</a>. It is an application of the&nbsp;<a title="Resource Interchange File Format" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resource_Interchange_File_Format">Resource Interchange File Format</a>&nbsp;(RIFF)&nbsp;<a title="Bitstream format" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bitstream_format">bitstream format</a>&nbsp;method for storing data in "chunks", and thus is also close to the&nbsp;<a title="8SVX" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/8SVX">8SVX</a>&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<a title="Audio Interchange File Format" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Audio_Interchange_File_Format">AIFF</a>&nbsp;format used on&nbsp;<a title="Amiga" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amiga">Amiga</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Apple Macintosh" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_Macintosh">Macintosh</a>&nbsp;computers, respectively. It is the main format used on&nbsp;<a title="Microsoft Windows" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsoft_Windows">Microsoft Windows</a>&nbsp;systems for raw and typically uncompressed audio. The usual bitstream encoding is the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Linear pulse-code modulation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linear_pulse-code_modulation">linear pulse-code modulation</a>&nbsp;(LPCM) format.</li>
<li><strong><a title="Web crawler" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_crawler">Web crawler</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; sometimes called a spider or spiderbot and often shortened to crawler, is an&nbsp;<a title="Internet bot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet_bot">Internet bot</a>&nbsp;that systematically browses the&nbsp;<a title="World Wide Web" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Wide_Web">World Wide Web</a>, typically for the purpose of&nbsp;<a title="Web indexing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_indexing">Web indexing</a>&nbsp;(<em>web spidering</em>).</li>
<li><strong><a title="Wi-Fi" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wi-Fi">Wi-Fi</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; is a family of wireless networking technologies, based on the&nbsp;<a title="IEEE 802.11" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IEEE_802.11">IEEE 802.11</a>&nbsp;family of standards, which are commonly used for&nbsp;<a title="Wireless LAN" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wireless_LAN">local area networking</a>&nbsp;of devices and&nbsp;<a title="Internet" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet">Internet</a>&nbsp;access.&nbsp;<em>Wi‑Fi</em>&nbsp;is a trademark of the non-profit&nbsp;<a title="Wi-Fi Alliance" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wi-Fi_Alliance">Wi-Fi Alliance</a>, which restricts the use of the term&nbsp;<em>Wi-Fi Certified</em>&nbsp;to products that successfully complete&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Interoperability Solutions for European Public Administrations" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interoperability_Solutions_for_European_Public_Administrations">interoperability</a>&nbsp;certification testing.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="X" class="mw-headline">X</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><strong><a title="XHTML" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/XHTML">XHTML</a></strong>&nbsp;&ndash; eXtensible HyperText Markup Language, is part of the family of&nbsp;<a title="XML" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/XML">XML</a>&nbsp;<a title="Markup language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Markup_language">markup languages</a>. It mirrors or extends versions of the widely used&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="HyperText Markup Language" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HyperText_Markup_Language">HyperText Markup Language</a>&nbsp;(HTML), the language in which&nbsp;<a title="Web page" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_page">Web pages</a>&nbsp;are formulated.</li>
</ul>
</br>

<h2> Timeline of the Consumer Computer Revolution</h2>

<table>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td class="bold">1975</td>
<td>Bill Gates and Paul Allen found the Microsoft Corporation.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">1976</td>
<td>The next year, Steve Jobs and Steve Wozniak form Apple Computers, Inc., and soon begin production of the Apple II, the first commercially successful, personal desktop computer.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">1981</td>
<td>Playing catch-up, IBM launches its Personal Computer, running Microsoft&rsquo;s MS-DOS operation system.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">1984</td>
<td>Apple introduces the Macintosh, the first personal computer utilizing a graphic user interface (GUI) and sold with numerous pre-installed, software applications.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">1991</td>
<td>Tim Berners-Lee, working at the CERN high-energy physics facility near Geneva, creates the first Web server, and the World Wide Web is born.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">1994</td>
<td>A mere three years later, Jeff Bezos founds Amazon.com.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">1994</td>
<td>That same year, the Intel Corporation introduces the Pentium microprocessor, which breaks new ground in both miniaturization and affordability, paving the way to the widespread adoption of laptops.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">1995</td>
<td>Microsoft releases the Windows 95 operating system &mdash;&thinsp;the grandparent to most present-day operation systems.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">1998</td>
<td>Four years after that, two Stanford grad students, Sergei Brin and Larry Page, create the Google search engine.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">2001</td>
<td>Apple introduces the iPod.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">2004</td>
<td>Mark Zuckerberg founds Facebook.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">2006</td>
<td>Hard on FB&rsquo;s heels, Twitter is launched by Jack Dorsey and others.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">2007</td>
<td>Apple&rsquo;s iPhone &mdash;&thinsp;the first smartphone &mdash;&thinsp;is released.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">2007</td>
<td>That same year, Netflix makes video streaming available to its DVD rental customers, sounding the death knell of the DVD &mdash;&thinsp;itself a technology only introduced in 1997!</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">2010</td>
<td>Apple releases the iPad, the first tablet-sized personal computer.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</br>

<h2> Timeline of the Theory of Computation and Electronic Digital Computers</h2>

<table>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td class="bold">1931</td>
<td>Kurt G&ouml;del publishes his first &ldquo;incompleteness theorem,&rdquo; one of the foundational mathematical theorems proving the logical possibility of a general purpose digital computer.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">1936</td>
<td>Inspired by G&ouml;del&rsquo;s incompleteness theorem, Alonzo Church (with help from his student Stephen Kleene) proves what later will become known as &ldquo;Church&rsquo;s Thesis&rdquo; (or the &ldquo;Church-Turing Thesis&rdquo;), namely, that a function is computable only if it is &ldquo;effectively calculable&rdquo; (later shown to be equivalent to calculable by a Turing machine).</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">1936</td>
<td>That same year, Alan Turing publishes &ldquo;On Computable Numbers, with an Application to the&nbsp;<cite>Entscheidungsproblem</cite>,&rdquo; the path-breaking paper proving the possibility of a &ldquo;universal machine&rdquo; (now known as a &ldquo;Turing machine&rdquo;), which is the abstract idea lying at the heart of every computer. In the same paper &mdash;&thinsp;as well as in another paper published in collaboration with Church that same year &mdash;&thinsp;Turing also proves that the answer to the Halting Problem (&ldquo;Is it possible to know in advance whether any given computation is finite?&rdquo;) is No.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">1936</td>
<td>That same year, Emil L. Post develops independently many of the same ideas as Church and Turing.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">1945</td>
<td>John Mauchly, J. Presper Eckert, and Arthur W. Burks design the ENIAC for the US Army; housed at the University of Pennsylvania, it is the world&rsquo;s first general purpose, re-programmable (&ldquo;Turing complete&rdquo;) electronic digital computer.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">1945</td>
<td>That same year, John von Neumann describes what later comes to be known as the &ldquo;von Neumann architecture,&rdquo; in which the program and data are both stored in the same space in memory; von Neumann architecture is a large advance beyond previous operating system architectures.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">1953</td>
<td>The RAND Corporation inaugurates the Johnniac &mdash;&thinsp;the first computer to run with an operating system based on von Neumann architecture.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">1957</td>
<td>Herbert A. Simon and Allen C. Newell introduce the General Problem Solver program, which forms the foundation of most future research in artificial intelligence.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">1958</td>
<td>John McCarthy publishes &ldquo;Programs with Common Sense,&rdquo; in which he outlines the hypothetical &ldquo;advice taker&rdquo; program which imitates human reasoning through a question-and-answer format; McCarthy will go on to invent the Lisp and ALGOL computer languages.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">1961</td>
<td>McCarthy introduces the idea of computer time-sharing.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="bold">1964</td>
<td>IBM&rsquo;s revolutionary System/360 mainframe computer hits the market.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
